--- Document Chunk 62 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 63 ---
The purpose of investigating railway accidents is to establish their cause s and 

--- Document Chunk 64 ---
the circumstances in which they occurred, with a view to preventing recurrence 

--- Document Chunk 65 ---
in the future, and to draw up suitable recommendations for reducing the risks of 

--- Document Chunk 66 ---
railway accidents.  In any event, this investigation is not concerned with 

--- Document Chunk 67 ---
apportioning blame or responsibility and is independent of any judicial inquiry. 

--- Document Chunk 68 ---
(Royal Decree 810/2007, of 22 June 2007, Title III, Article 21)

--- Document Chunk 307 ---
1. SUMMARY 

--- Document Chunk 308 ---
A serious accident occurred at 20:41 hours on 24  July 2013, at PK 84+413 of line 082 from Coto da 

--- Document Chunk 309 ---
Torre branch (Ourense) to A Grandeira branch (A Coruña), kilometre point  85.0, near Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 310 ---
Compostela station (A Coruña). This was due to derailment of all ve hicles of long -distance passenger 

--- Document Chunk 311 ---
train 150/151, belonging to Renfe Operadora. This had come from Madrid -Chamartín and was bound 

--- Document Chunk 312 ---
for Ferrol. 

--- Document Chunk 313 ---
The entire trainset was derailed causing catastrophic personal injuries and material damage. 

--- Document Chunk 314 ---
There were 80 fataliti es and many  seriously injured.  

--- Document Chunk 315 ---
Conclusion: The cause of the accident was excessive speed of the train (travelling at 179  km/h) on 

--- Document Chunk 316 ---
the curve leading in to A Grandeira branch (th e Angrois curve, speed limit 80  km/h). The driver was in 

--- Document Chunk 317 ---
breach of the requirements of the timetable of train 150/151 and of the Table of Maximum Speeds for 

--- Document Chunk 318 ---
line 082. 

--- Document Chunk 319 ---
As a contributory cause, it is noted that that the driver ’s attention was reduced  when he answered a 

--- Document Chunk 320 ---
service telephone call on the train from the train manager, which caused him not to brake sufficiently 

--- Document Chunk 321 ---
to reduce speed before entering that curve. 

--- Document Chunk 322 ---
Recommendations: 

--- Document Chunk 323 ---
Final addressee  Number Recommendation 

--- Document Chunk 324 ---
Adif 54/13-1 

--- Document Chunk 325 ---
Make it a rule that all speed reductions, from a certain 

--- Document Chunk 326 ---
deceleration onwards, must be marked at the track side 

--- Document Chunk 327 ---
by fixed speed limit signs.  

--- Document Chunk 328 ---
Adif 54/13-2 

--- Document Chunk 329 ---
For these situations (significant speed reductions), 

--- Document Chunk 330 ---
arrange to set up balises progressively which may help to 

--- Document Chunk 331 ---
control the speed of trains, so that they brake in case the 

--- Document Chunk 332 ---
speed limit for entry into the block section is lowered. 

--- Document Chunk 333 ---
Therefore, implement the necessary ASFA Digital 

--- Document Chunk 334 ---
(Automatic Braking and Announcement of Signals) 

--- Document Chunk 335 ---
systems.  

--- Document Chunk 336 ---
Renfe Operadora 54/13-3.1 

--- Document Chunk 337 ---
Reinforce the procedures set in the Renfe Operadora SMS 

--- Document Chunk 338 ---
so that safety -related defects detected at any level are 

--- Document Chunk 339 ---
referred to the departments with the prescribed function 

--- Document Chunk 340 ---
of analysing and considering them, thereby assuring 

--- Document Chunk 341 ---
effective preventive management. 

--- Document Chunk 342 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 343 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 344 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 345 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 346 ---

--- Document Chunk 354 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 355 ---
Page 9 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 356 ---
Dirección General de 

--- Document Chunk 357 ---
Ferrocarriles 

--- Document Chunk 358 ---
(National 

--- Document Chunk 359 ---
Directorate-General 

--- Document Chunk 360 ---
of Railways DGF) 

--- Document Chunk 361 ---
54/13-3.2 

--- Document Chunk 362 ---
The national railway safety authority  will ensure that 

--- Document Chunk 363 ---
Recommendation 54/13 -3.1 is extended to the other 

--- Document Chunk 364 ---
railway undertakings. 

--- Document Chunk 365 ---
DGF 54/13-4 

--- Document Chunk 366 ---
The national railway safety authority  should consider 

--- Document Chunk 367 ---
whether to reconvene the joint traffic safety committees, 

--- Document Chunk 368 ---
including active input from representatives from Adif and 

--- Document Chunk 369 ---
the railway undertakings, and under the authority’s 

--- Document Chunk 370 ---
supervision. These committees can analyse risk situations 

--- Document Chunk 371 ---
that can derive from  the interaction between driving, 

--- Document Chunk 372 ---
vehicle and track.  

--- Document Chunk 373 ---
DGF 54/13-5 

--- Document Chunk 374 ---
The process of c ommissioning new railway lines and 

--- Document Chunk 375 ---
alternative stretches should include a specific risk 

--- Document Chunk 376 ---
assessment. This should include identification and 

--- Document Chunk 377 ---
management of possible hazards driving from the 

--- Document Chunk 378 ---
interaction between subsystems, in normal and degraded 

--- Document Chunk 379 ---
operating conditions, and their links with the driving and 

--- Document Chunk 380 ---
traffic staff involved when a train is travelling from 

--- Document Chunk 381 ---
beginning to end of the line or alternative stretch, and its 

--- Document Chunk 382 ---
connection to the existing network. Also analyse the 

--- Document Chunk 383 ---
viability of the layout at the various construction stages.  

--- Document Chunk 384 ---
In justified cases, promote the application of such 

--- Document Chunk 385 ---
assessments to lines which are in service.  

--- Document Chunk 386 ---
DGF 54/13-6 

--- Document Chunk 387 ---
Make the necessary arrangements for communications 

--- Document Chunk 388 ---
with driving staff in the cab to take place safely and avoid 

--- Document Chunk 389 ---
possible distrac tions. Make these arrangements part of 

--- Document Chunk 390 ---
the general regulations and pass them on to the railway 

--- Document Chunk 391 ---
undertakings for inclusion in their safety management 

--- Document Chunk 392 ---
systems. 

--- Document Chunk 393 ---
Renfe Operadora 54/13-7.1 

--- Document Chunk 394 ---
Promote the progressive implementation of an audio 

--- Document Chunk 395 ---
recording system in drivers’ cabs. Assess the feasibility of 

--- Document Chunk 396 ---
adding a video recording system as well. 

--- Document Chunk 397 ---
DGF 54/13-7.2 

--- Document Chunk 398 ---
The national railway safety authority  will ensure that 

--- Document Chunk 399 ---
Recommendation 54/13 -7.1 is extended to the other 

--- Document Chunk 400 ---
railway undertakings. 

--- Document Chunk 401 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 402 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 403 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 404 ---

2. BASIC SEQUENCE OF EVENTS 

--- Document Chunk 416 ---
2.1. SEQUENCE OF EVENTS 

--- Document Chunk 417 ---
2.1.1. Details 

--- Document Chunk 418 ---
Date/time:    24.07.2013/20:41 

--- Document Chunk 419 ---
Place:   PK 84+413, 3.6 km from Santiago de Compostela station 

--- Document Chunk 420 ---
Line:    082 Coto da Torre Branch - A Grandeira Branch, km point 85.0 

--- Document Chunk 421 ---
Municipality:   Santiago de Compostela (Angrois District) 

--- Document Chunk 422 ---
Province:    A Coruña 

--- Document Chunk 423 ---
Autonomous Community: Galicia 

--- Document Chunk 424 ---
2.1.2. Description of events 

--- Document Chunk 425 ---
The events occurred at 20:41  hours on 24  July 2013, at PK 84+413 of Line 082, Coto da Torre 

--- Document Chunk 426 ---
branch - A Grandeira branch, km point 85.0, near Santiago de Compostela station. 

--- Document Chunk 427 ---
The Alvia Class 730 long-distance passenger train 150/151, run by Renfe Operadora, consisted of 

--- Document Chunk 428 ---
13 vehicles. It was coming from Madrid -Chamartín and bound for Ferrol (A Coruña). After making a 

--- Document Chunk 429 ---
scheduled stop at Ourense station with changeover of driver, it continued on its rout e via line 082 

--- Document Chunk 430 ---
(known as the Ourense – Santiago line). It departed from Ourense with a four minute delay. 

--- Document Chunk 431 ---
The train covered the first 78  km of the line  at an approximate speed of 200  km/h. The ASFA Digital 

--- Document Chunk 432 ---
system was working. All signals on its path indicated ‘track clear’.  

--- Document Chunk 433 ---
About 6000  m (PK 78+280) before the start of the curve leading to the A Grandeira branch (at 

--- Document Chunk 434 ---
PK 84+228, where speed of travel is restricted to 80 km/h), the driver answered a service call from the 

--- Document Chunk 435 ---
train manager (guard) on the corporate mobile telephone. 

--- Document Chunk 436 ---
The trainset continued along track 1 and passed caution signal E´7 (PK  80+619) of the A Grandeira 

--- Document Chunk 437 ---
branch. After noting that the signal was indicating ‘track clear’ to proceed on the main track, and at 

--- Document Chunk 438 ---
a speed close to 200  km/h, the driver  continued the telephone call with the train manager. This 

--- Document Chunk 439 ---
probably distracted his attention, and he did not start braking in time to adjust to the prescribed 

--- Document Chunk 440 ---
speed for the radius 402  m curve located from PK  84+228.  

--- Document Chunk 441 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 442 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 443 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 444 ---
A

--- Document Chunk 453 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 454 ---
Page 11 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 455 ---
The last sound of the telephone conver sation was recorded very close to signal E7 at the start of the 

--- Document Chunk 456 ---
branch (PK 84+176), which also indicated that the track was clear (100 seconds had passed since the 

--- Document Chunk 457 ---
start of the call). This is when the emergency brake was applied, as the signal was passed a t 

--- Document Chunk 458 ---
195 km/h. 

--- Document Chunk 459 ---
Train 150/151 was already very near the start of the curve (PK 84+228). It derailed on the curve, 

--- Document Chunk 460 ---
185 metres from the start, at PK 84+413, while travelling at 179 km/h. 

--- Document Chunk 461 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 462 ---
Tren 150-151 Train 150-151 

--- Document Chunk 463 ---
The three coaches of the trainset remained derailed and off line 1 on which they had been travelling.  

--- Document Chunk 464 ---
The first three were separated from the next two coaches by about 10  m, while those two were 

--- Document Chunk 465 ---
about 30 m away from the rest. The rear generator car caught fire. One of the coaches of the rear 

--- Document Chunk 466 ---
rake (the eighth) was pushed over the containing wall on to a nearby road.  

--- Document Chunk 467 ---
Both the main tracks of line 082 were blocked at the A Grandeira branch. A third track which passes 

--- Document Chunk 468 ---
next to the others at that point, but belongs to line 822 (Zamora - A Coruña), was also treated as out 

--- Document Chunk 469 ---
of service, to facilitate the work of rescue and repair, even though this track was unaffected by the 

--- Document Chunk 470 ---
accident. 

--- Document Chunk 471 ---
There was substantial material damage, mainly to rolling stock. Track  2 was not reopened to traffic 

--- Document Chunk 472 ---
until 26 July, while track 1 remained closed until 29 July.

2.1.3. Decision to open the investigation 

--- Document Chunk 488 ---
The Head of Accident Investigations of the Traffic Safety Directorate of Adif (the Spanish railway 

--- Document Chunk 489 ---
infrastructure administrative body) informed the secretary of the Railway Accident Investi gation 

--- Document Chunk 490 ---
Commission (CIAF), by telephone call at 21:11 hours on 24  July 2013, that the accident now under 

--- Document Chunk 491 ---
investigation had occurred. He also sent SMS messages to the other CIAF staff at 21:18.  

--- Document Chunk 492 ---
At the same time the Ministry of Development Sub -Secretariat also telephoned the CIAF Chairman and 

--- Document Chunk 493 ---
Secretary to inform them of the event and its gravity. They both immediately set out for Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 494 ---
Compostela. The Secretary arrived at the accident scene the same night. The Commission’s rail 

--- Document Chunk 495 ---
infrastructure expert join ed him after midnight. They immediately began analysis of what had 

--- Document Chunk 496 ---
happened with Adif and Renfe Operadora staff. Early next morning, the CIAF Chairman and one of the 

--- Document Chunk 497 ---
technical investigators arrived at the scene of the accident and joined the team already a t work. 

--- Document Chunk 498 ---
Article 21 et seq. of the Regulation on Traffic Safety on the Public Rail Network, which was approved 

--- Document Chunk 499 ---
by Royal Decree 810/2007 of 22  June 2007 (BOE No  162, of 7 July 2007), assign competence for the 

--- Document Chunk 500 ---
investigation of railway accidents and incidents to the Railway Accident Investigation Commission. 

--- Document Chunk 501 ---
In accordance with the provision of Article  21 of that Regulation, and as defined in Article  2, it is 

--- Document Chunk 502 ---
mandatory to investigate what has happened when the accident is serious.  

--- Document Chunk 503 ---
Under Article 23.1 of that Regulation, and in view of the exceptional features of this accident, the CIAF 

--- Document Chunk 504 ---
Chairman passed a resolution on 26  July 2013 appointing the CIAF Secretary as Chief Investigator. 

--- Document Chunk 505 ---
The Secretary, who has signed this report, then worked with the two investigators belonging to this 

--- Document Chunk 506 ---
Commission. 

--- Document Chunk 507 ---
The members of the investigating team were the Secretariat technician referred to, plus: 

--- Document Chunk 508 ---
- the Traffic Safety Director of Adif, who delivered his personal report on 6  November 2013, 

--- Document Chunk 509 ---
signed, with due authority, by the Sub -Director of Rolling Stock and Traffic Safety Management 

--- Document Chunk 510 ---
and the head of accident investigation; and  

--- Document Chunk 511 ---
- the Traffic Safety Director of Renfe Operadora, who delivered his personal report on 

--- Document Chunk 512 ---
5 November 2013, signed jointly with the head of the accident technical in vestigation area.  

--- Document Chunk 513 ---
INECO, S.A., a publicly owned company, acting within the framework of an agreeme nt for the 

--- Document Chunk 514 ---
provision of support in investigating railway accidents signed with the Sub-Secretariat of the Ministry of 

--- Document Chunk 515 ---
Development, has carried out work in sup port of the accident investigation on behalf of the chief 

--- Document Chunk 516 ---
investigator. 

--- Document Chunk 517 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 518 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 519 ---

2.2. CIRCUMSTANCES OF THE ACCIDENT 

--- Document Chunk 532 ---
2.2.1. Railway staff involved 

--- Document Chunk 533 ---
The railway staff involved were mainly the train crew, belonging to Renfe Operadora. They consisted 

--- Document Chunk 534 ---
of: 

--- Document Chunk 535 ---
-  the driver of train 150/151, whose registration number was 8945362; and  

--- Document Chunk 536 ---
-  the manager of train 150/151, with the duties of guard, registration number 9610643. 

--- Document Chunk 537 ---
Off-duty staff also travelling were the driver who had driven th e train on the Medina del 

--- Document Chunk 538 ---
Campo-Ourense route, one safety officer and two employees of the catering firm, who were working in 

--- Document Chunk 539 ---
the restaurant car. 

--- Document Chunk 540 ---
2.2.2. Rolling stock 

--- Document Chunk 541 ---
Train 150/151 leaves Madrid-Chamartín at 15:00 hours daily (it has another number at weekends). It is a 

--- Document Chunk 542 ---
double rake. It arrives at Ourense at 19:51 hours, where the two rakes are divided. One goes to Ferrol 

--- Document Chunk 543 ---
(with the same number), where it is scheduled to arrive at 22:36 hours. The other goes to Pontevedra 

--- Document Chunk 544 ---
(renumbered as a different train). Departure time from Ourense station is 20:01 hours; arrival at 

--- Document Chunk 545 ---
Santiago de Compostela according to the timetable is 20:41 hours. 

--- Document Chunk 546 ---
On the day of the accident, train 150/151 was made up of number 730.012, i.e. rake 12, Class 730, 

--- Document Chunk 547 ---
manufactured by the Talgo -Bombardier Consortium and consisting of 13 vehicles: two power cars at 

--- Document Chunk 548 ---
either end, followed by two generator cars at either end, eight passenger coaches and a restaurant car. 

--- Document Chunk 549 ---
Both the power cars and the generator cars had bogies (two and one, respectively). The other coaches 

--- Document Chunk 550 ---
had simple independent wheelsets. 

--- Document Chunk 551 ---
The train had 264 seats, divided into 48 club class (including one place for people of reduced mobility - 

--- Document Chunk 552 ---
PMR) and 216 in tourist class. The seats were in two coaches for club class and six for tourist class. As 

--- Document Chunk 553 ---
specified in the train logbook, it is 185 m long and weighs 382 tons. The total number of axles is 22. 

--- Document Chunk 554 ---
Class 730 is a conversion of Class 130 (only suitable for travel on electrified lines). Class 130 is also 

--- Document Chunk 555 ---
manufactured by the Talgo -Bombardier Consortium. To convert it, they modified two end passenger 

--- Document Chunk 556 ---
coaches to a ccommodate one generator unit each. The electricity generated by these powered the 

--- Document Chunk 557 ---
electric motors of the power cars, allowing the class to travel on unelectrified lines. 

--- Document Chunk 558 ---
The main technical features of Class 730 are as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 559 ---
 Wheels adjustable for travel on any tracks of standard or Iberian gauge. 

--- Document Chunk 560 ---
 Power supply from an overhead power line at 25 kV AC or 3 kV DC. It can run on 

--- Document Chunk 561 ---
unelectrified lines, due to the presence of the generator cars described above. 

--- Document Chunk 562 ---
 Equipped with ASFA Digital and ERTMS/ETCS , although  shortly after commencement of 

--- Document Chunk 563 ---
commercial operation on line  082 (Ourense -Santiago), due to problems of reliability and 

--- Document Chunk 564 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 565 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 566 ---

availability with the ERTMS configuration of this Class 730 on this line, the operator (Renfe 

--- Document Chunk 579 ---
Operadora) applied to operate under a tracks ide signal block (BSL) with the protection of 

--- Document Chunk 580 ---
ASFA Digital. It received authorisation to do this from  Adif. The Madrid - Olmedo 

--- Document Chunk 581 ---
high-speed route operates with ERTMS. 

--- Document Chunk 582 ---
 Where the route permits, Renfe Operadora is authorised to operat e on lines of standard 

--- Document Chunk 583 ---
gauge (1 435 mm) with ERTMS switched on, at a maximum speed of 240 km/h. On lines of 

--- Document Chunk 584 ---
Iberian gauge (1 668 mm), its maximum speed is 220  km/h. Finally, irrespective of gauge, 

--- Document Chunk 585 ---
it operates with ASFA at a maximum speed of 200 km/h. If the line is not electrified (diesel 

--- Document Chunk 586 ---
power), the maximum speed is 180 km/h.

2.2.3. Description of infrastructure and signalling 

--- Document Chunk 643 ---
2.2.3.1. Madrid-Ferrol route 

--- Document Chunk 644 ---
Train 150/151 runs between Madrid and Ferrol on lines with different features, detailed below:  

--- Document Chunk 645 ---
Line 080 Madrid-Chamartín - Valladolid-Campo Grande 

--- Document Chunk 646 ---
From Madrid-Chamartín (PK 0+800) to point at PK 133+900 in Olmedo, where it links with line 074. 

--- Document Chunk 647 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 648 ---

--- Document Chunk 661 ---
This is a double high -speed track. It is electrified (25 kV) and has the standard gaug e. It has BSL, 

--- Document Chunk 662 ---
ERTMS/ETCS level 1 and back-up ASFA, and a GSM-R communications system. 

--- Document Chunk 663 ---
Olmedo high-speed line 074, point at PK 133+900 - Medina del Campo changeover 

--- Document Chunk 664 ---
The point at PK 133+900 on line 080 is PK 0+000 of line 074. That line is 19.9 km long and links 

--- Document Chunk 665 ---
Olmedo with the gauge changeover at Medina del Campo. It leaves from there on the Iberian gauge to 

--- Document Chunk 666 ---
line 820. 

--- Document Chunk 667 ---
It has BSL, ASFA and a GSM -R communications system. From the beginning (PK 0+000) to PK 3+312, 

--- Document Chunk 668 ---
the route runs in a double electrified track of standard gauge. From this point, it is a single track to 

--- Document Chunk 669 ---
Medina del Campo. 

--- Document Chunk 670 ---
Line 820 Medina del Campo – Zamora 

--- Document Chunk 671 ---
The train leaves the changeover on Iberian gauge at PK 0+000 on line 820. It goes along this line to 

--- Document Chunk 672 ---
Zamora, a distance of 89.5 kilometres of Iberian gauge single track. The track is not electrified. It has 

--- Document Chunk 673 ---
automatic clearance block for single track (BLAU) with central traffic control (CTC), local control (ML) 

--- Document Chunk 674 ---
and ASFA. There is no track-train radio telephony. 

--- Document Chunk 675 ---
Line 822 Zamora - A Coruña 

--- Document Chunk 676 ---
At Zamora, PK 89+500 of line 820 is PK 0+000 of line 822.  

--- Document Chunk 677 ---
The train runs along this line to Ourense station, a distance of  248.9 kilometres. The route continues 

--- Document Chunk 678 ---
with a single track on the Iberian gauge. It is not electrified, but has CTC, local control and ASFA. 

--- Document Chunk 679 ---
There is no track-train radiotelephony. Between Zamora and Puebla de Sanabria (106.9 km), the track 

--- Document Chunk 680 ---
has BLAU. Between Puebla de Sanabria and Ourense, it has an automatic block for single track (BAU). 

--- Document Chunk 681 ---
The train’s two rakes are separated at Ourense station. The rake bound for Ferrol continues to transit 

--- Document Chunk 682 ---
line 822, now electrified (3 kV). After 1 km, it reaches the Coto da  Torre branch, where it moves on to 

--- Document Chunk 683 ---
line 082. 

--- Document Chunk 684 ---
Line 082 Coto da Torre branch - A Grandeira branch km point 85.0 

--- Document Chunk 685 ---
As explained in greater detail in the sections below, this line is a component of the future Madrid - A 

--- Document Chunk 686 ---
Coruña high speed line. As such, it has t he design features of high speed, a double track and 25 kV 

--- Document Chunk 687 ---
electrification. It has been temporarily laid to the Iberian gauge, although it has multi -purpose sleepers 

--- Document Chunk 688 ---
to allow a quick change to standard gauge when the circumstances warrant it . It has BSL, 

--- Document Chunk 689 ---
ERTMS/ETCS level 1, except at its beginning and end, and back -up ASFA. The communications system 

--- Document Chunk 690 ---
is GSM-R.  

--- Document Chunk 691 ---
It ends at PK 85+000, at the A Grandeira branch, where it again connects to line 822. It leads to A 

--- Document Chunk 692 ---
Coruña via Santiago de Compostela station.

2.2.3.2.  Line 082 Coto da Torre branch - A Grandeira branch km point 85.0 

--- Document Chunk 749 ---
2.2.3.2.1. Infrastructure and track 

--- Document Chunk 750 ---
As described, the line consists of double track on the Iberian gauge, laid on multi -purpose concrete 

--- Document Chunk 751 ---
sleepers, grade PR-01. The track is type 60E1 and the catenary voltage 25 kV. Maximum slope is 25‰ 

--- Document Chunk 752 ---
and there are 31 tunnels  and 35 viaducts, the joint length of which accounts for nearly 60% of the 

--- Document Chunk 753 ---
route.

--- Document Chunk 772 ---

2.2.3.2.2. Control and signalling systems 

--- Document Chunk 817 ---
Line 082, Coto da Torre b ranch - A Grandeira branch, km point 85.0, has a block via trackside signal  

--- Document Chunk 818 ---
(BSL). The central traffic control (CTC), managed from the Adif Regulation and Control Centre (CRC) 

--- Document Chunk 819 ---
at the high -speed control post of Madrid’s Atocha station does not cover either branches (Coto da 

--- Document Chunk 820 ---
Torre or A Grandeira). These, with the adjacent Ourense and Santiago de Compostela stations, are 

--- Document Chunk 821 ---
managed from the Ourense control post when they are under central control. Nevertheless, both are 

--- Document Chunk 822 ---
operable under local control, when operatio ns are carried out from Ourense and Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 823 ---
Compostela stations respectively.  

--- Document Chunk 824 ---
The line has level 1 ERTMS/ETCS. In the direction of travel of the train (from Ourense to Santiago), this 

--- Document Chunk 825 ---
covers from PK 1+845 to PK 80+069. In the opposite direction, ERTMS is established from PK 84+200 to 

--- Document Chunk 826 ---
PK 7+206. As a back-up, ASFA is installed throughout the route. 

--- Document Chunk 827 ---
The point of the derailment (PK 84+413) is near the end of the line, at the A Grandeira branch. This is 

--- Document Chunk 828 ---
already beyond the stretch fitted with ERTMS. Hence at this point traffic is managed from the central 

--- Document Chunk 829 ---
control post at Ourense or, failing this, from Santiago de Compostela station when under local control.  

--- Document Chunk 830 ---
So there are three electronic interlocking limits laid out on the Ourense -Santiago section, which govern 

--- Document Chunk 831 ---
operations on this line. In the train’s direction of travel, the Ourense electronic interlocking system 

--- Document Chunk 832 ---
applies from the start of that station to PK 1+845 (the point where the ERTMS towards Santiago 

--- Document Chunk 833 ---
commences). The O Irixo interlocking system (with ERTMS) covers from the previous point to 

--- Document Chunk 834 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 835 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 836 ---

--- Document Chunk 876 ---

--- Document Chunk 877 ---
branches and Santiago station itself, all of which, as commented, are controlled from Ourense control 

--- Document Chunk 878 ---
post, when in central control mode, or from Santiago de Compostela s tation wh en in local control 

--- Document Chunk 879 ---
mode. 

--- Document Chunk 880 ---
More specifically, the derailment occurred in the A Grandeira branch, a subsection controlled by the 

--- Document Chunk 881 ---
Santiago de Compostela interlocking system. Access to the branch via track 1 of line 082, in the direction 

--- Document Chunk 882 ---
of the derailment (from Ourense to Santiago) is protected by entry signal E7 (PK 84+176) which, in turn, 

--- Document Chunk 883 ---
is announced by caution signal E´7 (PK 80+619). 

--- Document Chunk 884 ---
E7 is a tall signal with three lights (green, yellow and red). It is on the right side in the direction of travel.  

--- Document Chunk 885 ---
It has a fixed board showing 50 (50 km/h for a diverging line, which is not the case) and a luminous 

--- Document Chunk 886 ---
direction display. It has balises beforehand (PK 83+876) and at the signal (PK 84+171). Its position is at 

--- Document Chunk 887 ---
the exit from the Santiago tunnel (no 31) and it is clearly visible. 

--- Document Chunk 888 ---
E´7 is a tall signal with three lights (of which only two are operative: green and yellow). It is on the 

--- Document Chunk 889 ---
right-hand side in the direction of travel. It has a fixed board showing 60 (60 km/h for a diverging line, 

--- Document Chunk 890 ---
which is not the case) and a lum inous direction indicator. It has a balise beforehand (PK 80+319) but 

--- Document Chunk 891 ---
not at the signal (not necessary). It is located a little before the entrance to the Marrozos tunnel 

--- Document Chunk 892 ---
(no 30) and is clearly visible.  

--- Document Chunk 893 ---
Associated with this signal (E´7), three boards have  been set up nearby, at PKs 80+086, 80+278 and 

--- Document Chunk 894 ---
80+398, located at catenary posts.

--- Document Chunk 896 ---
travel, are as follows:

--- Document Chunk 898 ---
no 30 (Marrozos). It marks the point where it is necessary to change from ASFA - high 

--- Document Chunk 899 ---
speed  to ASFA – conventional mode.

--- Document Chunk 901 ---
E7. It shows that near here falls within the scope of RGC (the General Traffic Regulation).

--- Document Chunk 906 ---

2.2.3.3. Railway traffic data 

--- Document Chunk 940 ---
According to the CIRTRA 2012 information system (Traffic per Track Section), Volume II, of Adif’s 

--- Document Chunk 941 ---
Traffic Department, the average weekly traffic transiti ng line 082 in 2012 was 90 trains: 26 

--- Document Chunk 942 ---
long-distance, 63 medium-distance and 1 service train. 

--- Document Chunk 943 ---
The long -distance services (trade name Alvia) serve the Madrid -Ferrol link. They are hauled by 

--- Document Chunk 944 ---
Class 730 locomotives, the same as the train involved in the acciden t. Two daily services run each way 

--- Document Chunk 945 ---
on working days, and one at weekends (two on Sundays between Santiago de Compostela and 

--- Document Chunk 946 ---
Madrid). 

--- Document Chunk 947 ---
The medium-distance services (trade name Avant) serve the A Coruña -Santiago-Ourense link and are 

--- Document Chunk 948 ---
hauled by Class 121s. In No vember 2013 seven daily Avant services were scheduled each way on 

--- Document Chunk 949 ---
working days. This was reduced to five at weekends. 

--- Document Chunk 950 ---
Class 121 locomotives are manufactured by the CAF-ALSTOM Consortium. They have adjustable wheels 

--- Document Chunk 951 ---
(for Iberian and standard gauges), although in this zone all trains always run on the Iberian gauge. The 

--- Document Chunk 952 ---
maximum speed of travel is 250 km/h, and they have ERTMS and ASFA. 

--- Document Chunk 953 ---

To communicate outside the train on line 082, Coto da Torre branch - A Grandeira branch, km point 85.0,

--- Document Chunk 972 ---

--- Document Chunk 973 ---

--- Document Chunk 974 ---

--- Document Chunk 975 ---
To communicate inside the train, there is int ernal telephony for the driver to communicate with the 

--- Document Chunk 976 ---
crew. The personnel on duty on the train (train manager and driver) can also use the corporate mobile 

--- Document Chunk 977 ---
telephone. This enables them to communicate with each other and also outside, in limited form, and if 

--- Document Chunk 978 ---
necessary.

2.2.5. Activation of the railway contingency plan  

--- Document Chunk 994 ---
According to the information supplied by the Ministry of Development’s Emergencies and Crisis Coordination 

--- Document Chunk 995 ---
and Management Unit, by Renfe Operadora and by Adif, the sequence of actions was as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 996 ---
24 July 2013 

--- Document Chunk 997 ---
After the accident, at 20:42 hours, the driver of train 150/151 reported what had happened via GSM -R 

--- Document Chunk 998 ---
from the driving desk (in the head power car) to CRC Atocha. From this time on, the emergency 

--- Document Chunk 999 ---
protocols of Renfe Operadora and Adif, and th e coordination procedures between them, came into 

--- Document Chunk 1000 ---
action in order to implement the measures envisaged as necessary in support of the emergency. 

--- Document Chunk 1001 ---
Pursuant to these, CRC Atocha reported what had happened to 112, to the 24h Network Management 

--- Document Chunk 1002 ---
Centre (CGR24) and to the Adif control post at Ourense. 

--- Document Chunk 1003 ---
At 20:45 hours Adif CGR24 informed the Adif control post in León and the Renfe Operadora Operations 

--- Document Chunk 1004 ---
and Civil Defence Centre (CECON). After a chain of communications, Renfe Operadora convened its 

--- Document Chunk 1005 ---
crisis cell and activated the emergency protocol. The cell for assistance with communication media was 

--- Document Chunk 1006 ---
set up for 24 hours. Adif, in turn, launched its contingency plan. 

--- Document Chunk 1007 ---
In addition to tracks 1 and 2 of line 082 (Ourense -Santiago), which the accident blocked, the Ourense 

--- Document Chunk 1008 ---
control post decided to suspend traffic on the tracks of the conventional network in the area, to allow 

--- Document Chunk 1009 ---
risk-free action by people and equipment. 

--- Document Chunk 1010 ---
At 21:20 hours Renfe Operadora and Adif began to establish an alternative transport plan to minimise, 

--- Document Chunk 1011 ---
as far as possible, the consequences of the severing of lines for trains which were already travelling on 

--- Document Chunk 1012 ---
them, or were scheduled to do so. 

--- Document Chunk 1013 ---
Adif deployed major human and material resources. It mobili sed three workshop trains and heavy 

--- Document Chunk 1014 ---
track machinery in order to start work to repair the line, in  so far as it was authorised to do so.  

--- Document Chunk 1015 ---
Renfe Operadora also activated the major accidents protocol with reference to the compulsory 

--- Document Chunk 1016 ---
passenger insurance taken out with the insurance company, Allianz. It activated the protocol for 

--- Document Chunk 1017 ---
looking after casualties and family members, by opening a helpline to attend to  family members, 

--- Document Chunk 1018 ---
manage the information, requests for removals and psychological support. Later, on 29  July, an office 

--- Document Chunk 1019 ---
was set up in Madrid to look after the families of those i njured in the acciden t, with a procedure for 

--- Document Chunk 1020 ---
assisting family members with travel, with the cooperation of the airline, Iberia. 

--- Document Chunk 1021 ---
25 July 2013 

--- Document Chunk 1022 ---
At 03:10 hours the judge authorised access to the accident zone for personnel not belonging to the 

--- Document Chunk 1023 ---
emergency services (Adif, Renfe Operadora, CIAF, etc.). Renfe Operadora used large cranes to start to 

--- Document Chunk 1024 ---
clear damaged rolling stock from the track. It removed the first coach of the trainset at 07:25 hours. 

--- Document Chunk 1025 ---
At 12:52 hours, removal of that rolling stock began by road to a fi eld at A Escravitude (a locality near 

--- Document Chunk 1026 ---
Santiago de Compostela), where it remained in judicial custody. 

--- Document Chunk 1027 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1028 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1029 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1030 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 1031 ---
MINISTRY OF 

--- Document Chunk 1032 ---

--- Document Chunk 1041 ---
At 15:45 hours, after preliminary investigation work in situ, Adif began to repair track 1. 

--- Document Chunk 1042 ---
26 July 2013 

--- Document Chunk 1043 ---
At 05:00 hours, traffic was restored on the adjac ent conventional track with ‘proceed with caution ’ in 

--- Document Chunk 1044 ---
force at the place of the accident. Trains were authorised to pass at ordinary speed at 07:30 hours. At 

--- Document Chunk 1045 ---
the same time, traffic was restored on track 2 of line 082  involved in the accident. A speed limit  of 

--- Document Chunk 1046 ---
30 km/h applied to pass through the accident zone. 

--- Document Chunk 1047 ---
28 July 2013 

--- Document Chunk 1048 ---
At 06:45 hours Renfe Operadora removed the last rolling stock from track 1. This was the head power car. 

--- Document Chunk 1049 ---
This left the track unobstructed. Adif proceeded with the repair works. 

--- Document Chunk 1050 ---
29 July 2013 

--- Document Chunk 1051 ---
At 06:15 hours, the speed limit on track 2 was lifted. At 07:25 hours, traffic was restored to track 1, 

--- Document Chunk 1052 ---
with a 30 km/h speed limit through the accident zone. That limit remains in force on the date of this 

--- Document Chunk 1053 ---
report. 

--- Document Chunk 1054 ---
2.2.6. Activation of emergency plan by the public services  

--- Document Chunk 1055 ---
On 24 July 2013, after the accident, Adif alerted the Galicia Emergency Centre (112) to mobilise the 

--- Document Chunk 1056 ---
National Police, Guardia Civil, Local Police, Civil Defence, Red Cross, Fire Brigade and other healthcare 

--- Document Chunk 1057 ---
services to go to the scene of the accident. 

--- Document Chunk 1058 ---
As it happened, the main police headquarters, Guardia Civil and Local Police of Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 1059 ---
Compostela, had drawn up safety arrangements for that night. The main purpose of this was to 

--- Document Chunk 1060 ---
guarantee normal progress of all the activities planned for th e celebration of Galicia Day and the 

--- Document Chunk 1061 ---
festival of St. James the Apostle. This plan made it possible to move over 140 police personnel to the 

--- Document Chunk 1062 ---
zone of the accident by 21:15 hours. Parallel to the police deployment, the Fire Brigade and Civil 

--- Document Chunk 1063 ---
Defence were involved. 

--- Document Chunk 1064 ---
On the other hand, the Xunta (Government) of Galicia activated its emergency plan entitled Territorial 

--- Document Chunk 1065 ---
Civil Defence Plan of the Autonomous Community of Galicia ‘PLATERGA.’ Level 2 of this plan mobilised 

--- Document Chunk 1066 ---
all the resources required for this eventuality.  

--- Document Chunk 1067 ---
Therefore, according to Galician Government figures, more than 3000 personnel took part in the operation 

--- Document Chunk 1068 ---
launched in response to the accident: national police; members of the Guardia Civil, local police; firefighters 

--- Document Chunk 1069 ---
from seven different fire stations in Galicia; members of 26 Civil Defence groups; psychologists and 

--- Document Chunk 1070 ---
healthcare professionals from six hospitals, professionals from the Judicial Authority, professionals from the 

--- Document Chunk 1071 ---
Emergency Centre, and members of the Red Cross (staff and volunteers). 

--- Document Chunk 1072 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1073 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1074 ---

2.2.7. Structures at the accident location 

--- Document Chunk 1090 ---
At the time of the accident, no construction work was in progress on or near the track. There were no 

--- Document Chunk 1091 ---
temporary speed limits in the zone. 

--- Document Chunk 1092 ---
2.3. CASUALTIES (DEAD AND INJURED) AND MATERIAL DAMAGE  

--- Document Chunk 1093 ---
2.3.1. Casualties (dead and injured) 

--- Document Chunk 1094 ---
According to the information supplied by Renfe Operadora, 221 tickets for Santiago de Compostela, or 

--- Document Chunk 1095 ---
stations beyond, were sold for train 150/151. These tickets were for persons older than four years old 

--- Document Chunk 1096 ---
since no ticket is required for children up to the age of four. 

--- Document Chunk 1097 ---
Service personnel, who need no tickets, were also travelling on the t rain. Travellers on the 

--- Document Chunk 1098 ---
Ourense-Santiago route included a safety officer, the off -duty driver who had driven the train on the 

--- Document Chunk 1099 ---
Medina del Campo -Ourense route, two people working in t he cafeteria, the train manager and the 

--- Document Chunk 1100 ---
train driver. In total these were six people. Hence it is deduced that 227 people were travelling on the 

--- Document Chunk 1101 ---
train (ticketed + service), plus an indeterminate number of children younger than four years old.  

--- Document Chunk 1102 ---
To establish the number of fatalities, the Traffic Safety Regulation for the Public Railway Network, as 

--- Document Chunk 1103 ---
amended by Royal Decree 918/2010, of 16 July 2010, in line with the criterion of the European Safety 

--- Document Chunk 1104 ---
Directive, defines a fatality as any person who dies as a result  of an accident immediatel y or within 

--- Document Chunk 1105 ---
30 days. A seriously injured person is someone who spent more than 24 hours in hospital because of an 

--- Document Chunk 1106 ---
accident. 

--- Document Chunk 1107 ---
No official list of victims is available. Nevertheless, as an indication, at the end of August, Santiago d e 

--- Document Chunk 1108 ---
Compostela Magistrates’ Court 3 put the number of people affected by the accident at 226, of whom 

--- Document Chunk 1109 ---
79 were fatalities and 147 injured. Later Renfe Operadora notified the death of a person, which 

--- Document Chunk 1110 ---
brought the number of fatalities to 80 (including two crew m embers) and 152 those otherwise affected 

--- Document Chunk 1111 ---
by the accident. 

--- Document Chunk 1112 ---

2.3.2.3. Damage to third parties 

--- Document Chunk 1170 ---
Projectiles - pieces of track and train - caused damage to nearby buildings which awaits valuation. 

--- Document Chunk 1171 ---
2.3.3. Time lost through track blockage 

--- Document Chunk 1172 ---
At 05:00 hours on 26 July, traffic resumed on the conventional track (line 822) with ‘proceed with caution’ 

--- Document Chunk 1173 ---
in force in the accident zone. Thus this track was blocked for around 32 hours. Authority was given to pass 

--- Document Chunk 1174 ---
at normal speed at 07:30 hours on the same day. At the same time, traffic resumed on track 2 of line 082, 

--- Document Chunk 1175 ---
on which the accident occurred. The speed limit was 30 km/h through the accident zone. Thus track 2 was 

--- Document Chunk 1176 ---
blocked for around 35 hours. 

--- Document Chunk 1177 ---
At 06:15 hours on 29 July, the speed limit on track 2 was cancelled. At 07:25 hours, traffic resumed on 

--- Document Chunk 1178 ---
track 1, limited to 30 km/h through the accident zone. Thus this track had been blocked for 4 days and 

--- Document Chunk 1179 ---
11 hours.  

--- Document Chunk 1180 ---
According to  Adif, a total of 29 trains (27 passenger and 2 goods) were affected, either through 

--- Document Chunk 1181 ---
diversion on to other lines or by transfer of their passengers by road for part of their journey. 

--- Document Chunk 1182 ---
Total delay was 699 minutes. On 24 July, 7 trains were delayed 90 minutes ; on 25 July , 18 trains 

--- Document Chunk 1183 ---
(including 2 goods) were delayed 483 minutes; and on 26 July , 4 trains were delayed 126 

--- Document Chunk 1184 ---
minutes.  

--- Document Chunk 1185 ---
2.4. EXTERNAL CIRCUMSTANCES 

--- Document Chunk 1186 ---
The event occurred in daytime. Weather conditions were good. 

--- Document Chunk 1187 ---
The 24th of July is the eve of the feast of St. Jam es the Apostle and Galicia National Day. It also marks 

--- Document Chunk 1188 ---
annual festivals in the city of Santiago de Compostela, capital of the Autonomous Community of Galicia.

--- Document Chunk 1210 ---
Answers to the judge’s questions 

--- Document Chunk 1211 ---
- He was going calmly until he reached the curve.  

--- Document Chunk 1212 ---

--- Document Chunk 1213 ---
- At point 83+400 [ he really means 84+ 300], where the speed change signal is, he should have 

--- Document Chunk 1214 ---
been travelling at 80 km/h. 

--- Document Chunk 1215 ---
- The speed reduction is before [is made before] and everyone does it where he considers it appropriate. 

--- Document Chunk 1216 ---
Personally, he takes the caution signal [E´7], about 4 km before, as the reference point for braking. 

--- Document Chunk 1217 ---
- He was going at around 180-190 km/h when the accident occurred. 

--- Document Chunk 1218 ---
- He cannot explain why he did not reduce speed. 

--- Document Chunk 1219 ---
- 4 km is covered very quickly at 200 km/h. 

--- Document Chunk 1220 ---
- The signal was at green. 

--- Document Chunk 1221 ---
- The train was running 2 or 3 minutes late. 

--- Document Chunk 1222 ---
- He has never received warnings or penalties. 

--- Document Chunk 1223 ---

--- Document Chunk 1224 ---
received no penalty for it. 

--- Document Chunk 1225 ---
- The company checks, carries out speed checking scans to detect speeding. 

--- Document Chunk 1226 ---

--- Document Chunk 1227 ---

--- Document Chunk 1228 ---
- Each driver has a copy of the train timetable. These are documents  which all the drivers have. He  

--- Document Chunk 1229 ---
too, has an updated timetable which is his own. 

--- Document Chunk 1230 ---
- On the high -speed lines they are [ also] issued with a ‘train logbook ’ which shows precautions, 

--- Document Chunk 1231 ---
restrictions, anomalies etc.  

--- Document Chunk 1232 ---

Answers to the judge’s questions  

--- Document Chunk 1443 ---
- He is not a friend of the driver. It is purely a working relationship. 

--- Document Chunk 1444 ---
- He is the train manager on the route. They used to be known as conductors.  

--- Document Chunk 1445 ---
- He works for Renfe Operadora. 

--- Document Chunk 1446 ---
- His job is to check passengers getting on and off the train. He checks the passengers’ tickets. 

--- Document Chunk 1447 ---
- He considers it worth reporting all incidents occurring on the train to the driver, as the driver is in 

--- Document Chunk 1448 ---
charge of the train.  

--- Document Chunk 1449 ---
- Communication with the driver [ on board the train ] can be face -to-face or by telephone. 

--- Document Chunk 1450 ---
Face-to-face means in person. Otherwise, where coverage exists, communication is by mobile 

--- Document Chunk 1451 ---
telephone. If there is an emergency and there is no mobile coverage, he walks to the cab, but 

--- Document Chunk 1452 ---
always uses the telephone first, since this is the quicker system. 

--- Document Chunk 1453 ---
- He called the driver to tell him he was taking people to Puentedeume [ where there was a 

--- Document Chunk 1454 ---
scheduled halt ] and wanted to know if the train would fit the track on the section next to the 

--- Document Chunk 1455 ---
passenger building. The driver confirmed to him that it would fit perfectly. 

--- Document Chunk 1456 ---
- He had never ordered the driver to enter the track of that section, because this was impossible.  

--- Document Chunk 1457 ---
- The call must have been before the accident. When the accident happened, his telephone was 

--- Document Chunk 1458 ---
already in his pocket.  

--- Document Chunk 1459 ---
- He could not remember at wha t point he had made the call. He had called because telephone 

--- Document Chunk 1460 ---
coverage existed at the time. Between Ourense and Santiago, there was full coverage over the 

--- Document Chunk 1461 ---
whole route, but coverage was poor from Santiago to A Coruña. 

--- Document Chunk 1462 ---

--- Document Chunk 1531 ---
3.2. SAFETY MANAGEMENT SYSTEMS 

--- Document Chunk 1532 ---
The European Directive on safety on t he Community’s railways (2004/49/EC) was transposed into 

--- Document Chunk 1533 ---
Spanish law by Royal Decree 810/2007, of 22 June 2007, which approved the Traffic Safety Regulation 

--- Document Chunk 1534 ---
of the National Public Rail Network. Annex V of the Directive prescribes the principal content of 

--- Document Chunk 1535 ---
accident and incident investigation reports. Paragraph 3.2 of this refers specifically to the traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 1536 ---
Management Systems (traffic SMS) of the companies involved in each accident. 

--- Document Chunk 1537 ---
The Safety Management Systems (SMS) in force at Adif and Renfe Operador a were analysed in 

--- Document Chunk 1538 ---
accordance with this Directive. This analysis took place in three stages. The first two describe the 

--- Document Chunk 1539 ---
contents of the traffic Safety Management Systems of both companies (Adif and Renfe Operadora). A 

--- Document Chunk 1540 ---
third deals with their specific application to this accident. 

--- Document Chunk 1541 ---
3.2.1. SMS of the infrastructure manager: Adif 

--- Document Chunk 1542 ---
3.2.1.1. Structure and content 

--- Document Chunk 1543 ---
The company Chairman formally approved the SMS on 6 April 2010. It first states that Article 9 of 

--- Document Chunk 1544 ---
Royal Decree 810/2007 requires that ‘the Rail Infrastructure Manager (Ad if) shall establish a Safety 

--- Document Chunk 1545 ---
Management System which shall guarantee, within the scope of its duties, that the rail system at least 

--- Document Chunk 1546 ---
meets the safety targets and standards and is adapted to the safety requirements prescribed in the 

--- Document Chunk 1547 ---
technical specifications for interoperability (TSIs) and technical specifications for approval, and that the 

--- Document Chunk 1548 ---
relevant parts of the safety methods (SM) are applied’. 

--- Document Chunk 1549 ---
Based on this, it proved necessary to adapt the traffic SMS, in force at Adif since August 2006, to the 

--- Document Chunk 1550 ---
new requirements specified in Royal Decree 810/2007. 

--- Document Chunk 1551 ---
The text quoted states the requirements and presentation format which Adif’s traffic SMS must meet. It 

--- Document Chunk 1552 ---
goes on to specify that it must guarantee control of all the risks posed by its own activity as manager of 

--- Document Chunk 1553 ---
the infrastructure and of the railway undertakings which operate on it, including maintenance services, 

--- Document Chunk 1554 ---
supply of equipment and deployment of contractors. 

--- Document Chunk 1555 ---
In order to adapt Adif’s traffic SMS to the above requirements of the Royal Decree, the document with 

--- Document Chunk 1556 ---
three titles listed below has been drawn up: 

--- Document Chunk 1557 ---
Title I: Requirements of the Safety Management System 

--- Document Chunk 1558 ---
This contains a description of the allocation of responsibilities within the Adif organisation. It explains 

--- Document Chunk 1559 ---
how safety management is controlled at the various le vels, how staff and their representatives 

--- Document Chunk 1560 ---
participate in the various safety bodies, and how continuous improvement of the Safety Management 

--- Document Chunk 1561 ---
System is assured.  

--- Document Chunk 1562 ---
It is structured into five chapters, the contents of which are as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 1563 ---
Chapter 1: Structure and assignment of responsibilities 

--- Document Chunk 1564 ---

3.2.1.2. Procedures 

--- Document Chunk 1675 ---
As supplementary infor mation, the procedures which may be thought to be directly or indirectly 

--- Document Chunk 1676 ---
relevant to this accident investigation are detailed below. They currently form part of the Adif traffic 

--- Document Chunk 1677 ---
Safety Management System. 

--- Document Chunk 1678 ---
 Procedure of the traffic safety management participa tory bodies -SGSC/OPG- (from Title I, 

--- Document Chunk 1679 ---
Chapter 3) 

--- Document Chunk 1680 ---
Approved in February 2009, it defines the bodies which facilitate active participation by all Adif 

--- Document Chunk 1681 ---
staff in the traffic SMS, their membership and functions. It governs their functioning and 

--- Document Chunk 1682 ---
establishes the n ecessary mechanisms to implement the measures they pass, in order to 

--- Document Chunk 1683 ---
guarantee control of risk and continuous improvement of traffic safety. 

--- Document Chunk 1684 ---
 Procedure for drafting annual traffic safety plans -SGSC/PASC- (from Title II, Chapter 1, 

--- Document Chunk 1685 ---
section 4) 

--- Document Chunk 1686 ---
Approved in Se ptember 2010, this prescribes a set form for annual traffic safety plans, covering 

--- Document Chunk 1687 ---
how they are drafted and the monitoring and correction of any non -conformities from it which 

--- Document Chunk 1688 ---
may arise. 

--- Document Chunk 1689 ---
 Procedure for management of traffic documents –SGSC/GDC- (from Title II, Chapter 2) 

--- Document Chunk 1690 ---
This was approved in February 2012. Its purpose is to ensure the availability and quality of the 

--- Document Chunk 1691 ---
current regulations published by Adif, established in the General Traffic Regulation. It is the 

--- Document Chunk 1692 ---
procedure for applying for them and publishing, distributing and handing them out in the necessary 

--- Document Chunk 1693 ---
familiarisation time for the people who have to enforce them in pursuit of their duties. 

--- Document Chunk 1694 ---
 Procedure for certification of compliance with the traffic safety conditions applicable to the 

--- Document Chunk 1695 ---
Control, Command and Signalling subsystem -SGSC/CCC- (from Title II, Chapter 3, section 5) 

--- Document Chunk 1696 ---
Approved in January 2012, this describes the process at the Traffic Safety Directorate (DSC) for 

--- Document Chunk 1697 ---
issuing the safety certificate of compliance of the Control, Command and Signalling subsy stem 

--- Document Chunk 1698 ---
with the applicable safety conditions, for lines, or routes thereon, belonging to the Public Rail 

--- Document Chunk 1699 ---
Network (REFIG). 

--- Document Chunk 1700 ---
 Procedure for inspecting conditions of travel during journeys in the cab -SGSC/ICC- (from Title II, 

--- Document Chunk 1701 ---
Chapter 3, section 10) 

--- Document Chunk 1702 ---
Approved in O ctober 2009, the procedure explains how to check, from the driver’s cab, 

--- Document Chunk 1703 ---
compliance by driving and traffic staff, preservation of the infrastructure and railway facilities 

--- Document Chunk 1704 ---
necessary for operation, the safety devices and appliances in use, their fitness for  circulation and 

--- Document Chunk 1705 ---
the provision of the necessary staff. 

--- Document Chunk 1706 ---
 Procedure for inspecting speed recorders -SGSC/IRV- (from Title II, Chapter 3, section 10)  

--- Document Chunk 1707 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1708 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1709 ---

--- Document Chunk 1721 ---
This procedure, approved in February 2011, is for the corroboration, by means of recorder 

--- Document Chunk 1722 ---
samples, of compliance with the speed limits set in the timetables, execution of the required halts 

--- Document Chunk 1723 ---
and the use and functioning of the signalling and braking systems (ASFA, ASFA Digital, ATP, LZB, 

--- Document Chunk 1724 ---
ERTMS). In general, the procedure checks whether the actions of driving staff a re appropriate in 

--- Document Chunk 1725 ---
response to the successive information given by the safety devices. It also verifies the perfect 

--- Document Chunk 1726 ---
working order of the other active signals from the static memory equipment. 

--- Document Chunk 1727 ---
 Procedure for managing defect repair – SGSC/GCA (from Title II, Chapter 3, section 11) 

--- Document Chunk 1728 ---
The procedure, approved in August 2011, was devised for the creation of the rules of action after 

--- Document Chunk 1729 ---
the detection of non -conformities to the requirements established and detected during 

--- Document Chunk 1730 ---
inspections, visits, surveys, audits etc., which w ere discovered by any officer with power or 

--- Document Chunk 1731 ---
authority to do so, in the course of his duties. These non -conformities may relate both to 

--- Document Chunk 1732 ---
breaches of the regulations and to railway installations and rolling stock. The remedial action will 

--- Document Chunk 1733 ---
be taken to solve real and/or potential defects at the source. 

--- Document Chunk 1734 ---
 Procedure for risk assessment and management –SGSC/EGR (from Title II, Chapter 3, section 12) 

--- Document Chunk 1735 ---
Approved in October 2009, this establishes the procedure for assessing risks of accidents, as a 

--- Document Chunk 1736 ---
method of management. It makes this one of the key elements of risk prevention policy. 

--- Document Chunk 1737 ---
Risk assessment is a method which allows quantification and classification of the risks deriving 

--- Document Chunk 1738 ---
from the Adif operation. Hence it is essential for it to be accepted and uniform for all. The a im is 

--- Document Chunk 1739 ---
that comparison and classification should be uniform and feasible. 

--- Document Chunk 1740 ---
 Procedure for technical investigation of railway accidents –SGSC/ITAF- (from Title II, Chapter 6) 

--- Document Chunk 1741 ---
Approved in October 2009, this establishes the main rules to obey in the railway acci dent 

--- Document Chunk 1742 ---
investigation (IAF) process by Adif. It also prescribes the relations between the railway 

--- Document Chunk 1743 ---
undertakings (RU) and Adif and the action taken by them in the process of obtaining field data 

--- Document Chunk 1744 ---
and subsequent writing of railway accident reports. 

--- Document Chunk 1745 ---
3.2.2. SMS of the railway undertaking: Renfe Operadora  

--- Document Chunk 1746 ---
3.2.2.1. Structure and content 

--- Document Chunk 1747 ---
With regard to the safety of transport by rail in Spain, Law 39/2003 of 17 November 2003 on the rail 

--- Document Chunk 1748 ---
sector requires railway undertakings to hold a safety certificate in order to operate. This proves  

--- Document Chunk 1749 ---
compliance with the set requirements ‘on the management of safety, driving and accompanyin g staff 

--- Document Chunk 1750 ---
and rolling stock, and on any others prescribed by regulation’ (Article 57.2). 

--- Document Chunk 1751 ---
The safety certificate consists of a Part A, which confirms approval of the ra ilway undertaking’s Safety 

--- Document Chunk 1752 ---
Management System, in accordance with the provisions of Article  15 and Annex  2 of Royal 

--- Document Chunk 1753 ---
Decree 810/2007, and a Part  B, certifying approval of the measures adopted by the railway 

--- Document Chunk 1754 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1755 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1756 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1757 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 1758 ---

--- Document Chunk 1768 ---
undertaking to comply with the specific requirement s necessary for the provision of services in a safe 

--- Document Chunk 1769 ---
way. 

--- Document Chunk 1770 ---
Renfe Operadora, specifically, holds the safety certificate issued by the Railway Directorate -General in 

--- Document Chunk 1771 ---
force since May 2011. It is valid for the whole network, for the carriage of passengers and go ods. It is 

--- Document Chunk 1772 ---
in force until May 2016. The first certificate was issued on 30 June 2006. 

--- Document Chunk 1773 ---
The Safety Management System consists of: the company’s organisation with safety -related skills; the 

--- Document Chunk 1774 ---
safety procedures applicable to safety -related processes; and the bod ies in which staff participate 

--- Document Chunk 1775 ---
concerning traffic safety. 

--- Document Chunk 1776 ---
Below there is a summary of the SMS manual, approved in March  2011, followed by a list of some 

--- Document Chunk 1777 ---
procedures which may have a bearing on this accident investigation. 

--- Document Chunk 1778 ---
The purposes of the manual are as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 1779 ---
 to describe the structure of the Safety Management System and highlight the responsibilities of 

--- Document Chunk 1780 ---
the people and departments that fulfil functions relating to traffic safety; 

--- Document Chunk 1781 ---
 to instruct all members of the organisation on system content and further t heir commitment to 

--- Document Chunk 1782 ---
safety policy, good practice and effective risk prevention; and  

--- Document Chunk 1783 ---
 to supply the necessary information to carry out system audits. 

--- Document Chunk 1784 ---
It is structured into 11 chapters with the following contents:

Annex III: List of basic documentation of the traffic Safety Management System  

--- Document Chunk 1863 ---
Annex IV: Tabl e of relations between the Manual and the basic traffic Safety Management System 

--- Document Chunk 1864 ---
documentation 

--- Document Chunk 1865 ---
This is designed to give an overall vision of the manual. It establishes traceability between the sections 

--- Document Chunk 1866 ---
of the Safety Management System manual, the general procedures referred to in them, and the 

--- Document Chunk 1867 ---
specific procedures developed from them. Furthermore, this Annex refers to other supplementary 

--- Document Chunk 1868 ---
documents which form part of the traffic SMS and are used as back-up to the manual content. 

--- Document Chunk 1869 ---
3.2.2.2. Procedures 

--- Document Chunk 1870 ---
The Renfe Operadora traffic SMS is supplemented by 21 general proce dures. These amplify the 

--- Document Chunk 1871 ---
safety-related processes. They establish directives, methods, action modes and responsibilities. There are 

--- Document Chunk 1872 ---
also 14 specific procedures relating to technical and human risk management. These develop the content of 

--- Document Chunk 1873 ---
the general procedure for risk management and establish how specifically to proceed or carry out specific 

--- Document Chunk 1874 ---
activities and actions. 

--- Document Chunk 1875 ---
As further information, details follow on the procedures which can be considered, directly or indirectly, 

--- Document Chunk 1876 ---
in the investigation of this accident because they currently form part of the traffic Safety Management 

--- Document Chunk 1877 ---
System of Renfe Operadora. 

--- Document Chunk 1878 ---
3.2.2.2.1. General procedures  

--- Document Chunk 1879 ---
 SMS-PG-04.- Internal audit of the SMS (system quality audits as per the SMS certification 

--- Document Chunk 1880 ---
directive) 

--- Document Chunk 1881 ---
This establishes the form in which internal audits of the traffic SMS are planned and executed. It 

--- Document Chunk 1882 ---
ensures that the executing auditors are competent. 

--- Document Chunk 1883 ---
 SMS-PG-07.- Risk management 

--- Document Chunk 1884 ---
This defines the process which Renfe Operadora follows to manage the railway risks inherent in 

--- Document Chunk 1885 ---
its activity. It covers hazard identification and the processes for updating logs of such risks.  

--- Document Chunk 1886 ---
 SMS-PG-09.- Rolling stock commissioning authorisation 

--- Document Chunk 1887 ---
The purpose of this document is to define the process whereby Renfe Operadora: 

--- Document Chunk 1888 ---
 guarantees its rolling stock’s compliance with the technical standards applicable to it for 

--- Document Chunk 1889 ---
its commissioning authorisation (European standar ds, national safety standards and 

--- Document Chunk 1890 ---
Renfe Operadora’s in-house standards); and 

--- Document Chunk 1891 ---
 obtains authorisation for commissioning from the national safety authority (NSA) and 

--- Document Chunk 1892 ---
other administrative permits authorising the rolling stock to run. 

--- Document Chunk 1893 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 1894 ---

 SMS-PG-14.- Management of c ertificates and authorisations of personnel performing traffic 

--- Document Chunk 1908 ---
safety-related tasks  

--- Document Chunk 1909 ---
Its aim is to establish rules of action which must be followed during the process of management 

--- Document Chunk 1910 ---
of personnel certificates and authorisations. These may be employees or out siders who are going 

--- Document Chunk 1911 ---
to fulfil functions related to railway traffic safety at Renfe Operadora. The scope of this procedure 

--- Document Chunk 1912 ---
excludes granting and renewal of driving licences. 

--- Document Chunk 1913 ---
 SMS-PG-15.- Inspection 

--- Document Chunk 1914 ---
This establishes the methods of the various inspecting bodi es within Renfe Operadora and 

--- Document Chunk 1915 ---
defines the rules of action to follow in each case. 

--- Document Chunk 1916 ---
 SMS-PG-16.- Defect management 

--- Document Chunk 1917 ---
The purpose of this procedure is to specify how Renfe Operadora identifies and manages defects 

--- Document Chunk 1918 ---
which may impinge on its safety objectives. 

--- Document Chunk 1919 ---
 SMS-PG-17.- Action by Renfe Operadora to investigate accidents and incidents 

--- Document Chunk 1920 ---
The purpose of this document is to establish the organisation and methods to apply in the 

--- Document Chunk 1921 ---
process of investigating accidents and certain incidents in compliance with the provisions of the 

--- Document Chunk 1922 ---
Law on the Rail Sector and the Safety Regulation. It also seeks to explain the action by Renfe 

--- Document Chunk 1923 ---
contained in the joint procedure for ‘Coordination and Collection of Data in Accident/Incident 

--- Document Chunk 1924 ---
Investigations’ approved by the Adif and Renfe Operadora Corpo rate Traffic Safety Directors on  

--- Document Chunk 1925 ---
20 January 2006. 

--- Document Chunk 1926 ---
 SMS-PG-18.- Follow-up and checking of recommendations deriving from accident and incident 

--- Document Chunk 1927 ---
investigation reports  

--- Document Chunk 1928 ---
This describes how Renfe Operadora should proceed to follow up and check the 

--- Document Chunk 1929 ---
recommendations  deriving from the technical investigation of accidents and incidents, and the 

--- Document Chunk 1930 ---
corresponding action.  

--- Document Chunk 1931 ---
 SMS-PG-19.- Management of traffic safety training 

--- Document Chunk 1932 ---
The purpose of this document is to define the process whereby Renfe Operadora: 

--- Document Chunk 1933 ---
 ascertains the training needs of its staff who perform traffic safety-related tasks; 

--- Document Chunk 1934 ---
 plans the necessary training and provides it to those staff-members; and 

--- Document Chunk 1935 ---
 evaluates the effectiveness of its training courses.

--- Document Chunk 1950 ---
3.2.2.2.2. Specific procedures 

--- Document Chunk 1951 ---
 SMS-PE-01.-Accompanied trains 

--- Document Chunk 1952 ---
The aim is to preven t risks incurred by driving staff during service, to correct malpractice by 

--- Document Chunk 1953 ---
checking the action of driving personnel and also observing the surroundings which could 

--- Document Chunk 1954 ---
impinge on driving (man - machine - organisation), to ensure good performance while trains are 

--- Document Chunk 1955 ---
running or during manoeuvres. 

--- Document Chunk 1956 ---
 SMS-PE-04.- Management of safety recorder content 

--- Document Chunk 1957 ---
The objective is to establish rules of action for the extraction, safekeeping, analysis and 

--- Document Chunk 1958 ---
processing of the information stored in the safety recorders. Based on this, its  purpose is to 

--- Document Chunk 1959 ---
adopt the appropriate preventive and remedial measures to manage the risk situations identified 

--- Document Chunk 1960 ---
during analysis of the recordings. 

--- Document Chunk 1961 ---
 SMS-PE-08.- Management of risks posed by the human factor  

--- Document Chunk 1962 ---
This sets forth the methodology for the identificat ion of hazards, analysis, evaluation and control 

--- Document Chunk 1963 ---
of risks due to human behaviour during the operating stage. It involves establishing safety 

--- Document Chunk 1964 ---
measures oriented towards mitigating and/or eliminating their consequences, as part of the 

--- Document Chunk 1965 ---
continuous improvement of the SMS. 

--- Document Chunk 1966 ---
 SMS-PE-13.- Safety surveys 

--- Document Chunk 1967 ---
A ‘safety survey’ is an inspection initiative, a sample taken in relation to set questions concerned 

--- Document Chunk 1968 ---
with traffic safety. Its purpose is to obtain the necessary information to assess the situation 

--- Document Chunk 1969 ---
regarding the survey topic and establish any necessary measures to resolve or improve it.  

--- Document Chunk 1970 ---
3.2.3. Application of the traffic Safety Management Systems to this accident 

--- Document Chunk 1971 ---
3.2.3.1. Regulation cab documentation   

--- Document Chunk 1972 ---
According to Adif Safety Directorate Notice 74, dated 9  December 2011, the route betw een Coto da 

--- Document Chunk 1973 ---
Torre branch and A Grandeira branch km point  85.0 (i.e. line 082, where the accident occurred) falls 

--- Document Chunk 1974 ---
within the regulatory scope of the Technical Operating Requirements for Traffic and Safety (PTO). 

--- Document Chunk 1975 ---
The end sections at Ourense and Santiago de C ompostela are governed by the General Traffic 

--- Document Chunk 1976 ---
Regulation. 

--- Document Chunk 1977 ---
Thus, in accordance with PTO Article 106, the ‘train logbook’ informs the driver about the requirements 

--- Document Chunk 1978 ---
relating to the running of the train, temporary speed limits and the composition and braking o f the 

--- Document Chunk 1979 ---
train. It also contains all other information which has to be passed to the driver. This logbook is unique 

--- Document Chunk 1980 ---
to each train and day of operation. 

--- Document Chunk 1981 ---
Nevertheless, the running of the train is covered by a document with a longer term of validity, called 

--- Document Chunk 1982 ---
the train timetable or timetable book. This contains the train number, the type of block on each 

--- Document Chunk 1983 ---

--- Document Chunk 2003 ---

--- Document Chunk 2005 ---
The train logbook shows that braking availability was 200%, although 155% was necessary, and that the 

--- Document Chunk 2006 ---
train was type 240 B (maximum speed for the type of rolling stock was 240 km/h, without considering 

--- Document Chunk 2007 ---
other restrictions). On that day (24  July) a temporary speed limit of 200 km/h was in place, only on 

--- Document Chunk 2008 ---
track 1. This had been imposed since 25  June 2012, between PK  77.6 and PK  80.1 of that line (082). 

--- Document Chunk 2009 ---
There were no other recorded limits or restrictions. 

--- Document Chunk 2010 ---
The train timetable (bo ok) for Alvia train 150/151  reflects that it had to stop for 10  minutes at 

--- Document Chunk 2011 ---
Ourense station. It was scheduled to depart from there at 20:01 hours and arrive at Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 2012 ---
Compostela station at 20:41 hours, where it was to stop for two minutes.  

--- Document Chunk 2013 ---
Still accord ing to the timetable, at the beginning of line 082 the maximum permitted speed is 

--- Document Chunk 2014 ---
110 km/h between Coto da Torre branch and PK 2+903. Between that point and PK 84+230, the 

--- Document Chunk 2015 ---
maximum speed at which this train could travel (dictated by its own rolling stock) w as 220 km/h. This 

--- Document Chunk 2016 ---
point marked the beginning of the Angrois bend (the place of the accident), where the timetable 

--- Document Chunk 2017 ---
shows a change of speed. This is limited to 80 km/h until the end of line 082 (A Grandeira branch km 

--- Document Chunk 2018 ---
point 85.0). It then continued (on anothe r line: 822) with another change of speed to 75 km/h as far 

--- Document Chunk 2019 ---
as Santiago de Compostela station. 

--- Document Chunk 2020 ---
Between Ourense and Coto da Torre branch, the timetable indicates that ASFA is in operation with 

--- Document Chunk 2021 ---
communication by radiotelephone (track-train: channel 62). Throughout line 082, i.e. between Coto da 

--- Document Chunk 2022 ---
Torre branch and PK 85.0 (A Grandeira branch), the timetable states that ERTMS/ETCS level 1 applies 

--- Document Chunk 2023 ---
with ASFA (as back -up). Communication is via GSM -R. However, i n reality, the ERTMS ends at 

--- Document Chunk 2024 ---
PK 80+069, as stated in previous sections.  

--- Document Chunk 2025 ---
Between PK 85.0 and Santiago station, apparently only ASFA is avail able with radiotelephony 

--- Document Chunk 2026 ---
(track-train: channel 64).  

--- Document Chunk 2027 ---
The Maximum Speed Table for line 082, ‘odd’ direction (Ourense to Santiago de Compostela), indicates 

--- Document Chunk 2028 ---
that the maximum sp eed for the stretch is 110 km/h from the beginning to  PK 2+903. From there to 

--- Document Chunk 2029 ---
PK 6+094, maximum speed is limited to 235 km/h. From there to PK 84+230 (start of the Angrois bend 

--- Document Chunk 2030 ---
and place of the accident), the maximum speed rises to  300 km/h, but is reduced  to 80 on the next 

--- Document Chunk 2031 ---
section to A Grandeira km point 85.0 (end of the line). The information given in the last paragraph also

3.2.3.2. Staff requirements 

--- Document Chunk 2057 ---
The driver of train 150/151 was born in 1961. He holds driving licence B and is aut horised under 

--- Document Chunk 2058 ---
Order FOM/2520/2006, of 27  July 2006 (Title V ‘Driving Staff ’). This is in force until 

--- Document Chunk 2059 ---
11 January 2019, by virtue of interim provision 8 of Order FOM/2872/2010, of 5  November 2010. 

--- Document Chunk 2060 ---
Driving licence B entitles him to operate and handle any clas s of railway vehicle on any line of the 

--- Document Chunk 2061 ---
Public Rail Network (RFIG), provided that he also holds the due authorisations specified below.  

--- Document Chunk 2062 ---
As the holder of that licence since 1 January 2007, he has held the employment grade of Leader Driver 

--- Document Chunk 2063 ---
within Renfe Oper adora since 1  July 2010. Before that, he was a Principal Train Driver from 

--- Document Chunk 2064 ---
30 June 2008. He had been a driver with the former RENFE from June  2003, and had previously 

--- Document Chunk 2065 ---
served as an assistant driver from October 2000. He joined that company in December 1982. 

--- Document Chunk 2066 ---
To maintain the driving licence, it is necessary to attend a triennial refresher course. He last attended 

--- Document Chunk 2067 ---
one of these in January 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 2068 ---
A periodic medical check -up is also obligatory to assess psychological and physical fitness. Given the 

--- Document Chunk 2069 ---
driver’s age, the interval for this is also three-yearly. His last check-up was in September 2010. 

--- Document Chunk 2070 ---
Another requirement of the above -mentioned regulations in force is that the driver must hold 

--- Document Chunk 2071 ---
authorisation to drive the corresponding rolling stock, and another to drive on a given line.  

--- Document Chunk 2072 ---
So the driver has held authorisation to drive rolling stock Class 730 since March 2013. He is also 

--- Document Chunk 2073 ---
authorised for other types of rolling stock (medium and long -distance passenger, suburban and 

--- Document Chunk 2074 ---
goods). The dates vary, but the oldest dates  are from 2002.  

--- Document Chunk 2075 ---
His authorisation to drive on line 082 (Coto da Torre branch – A Grand eira branch) dates from 

--- Document Chunk 2076 ---
January 2012. He has also been authorised for other RFIG lines from different dates, the oldest being 

--- Document Chunk 2077 ---
2004. 

--- Document Chunk 2078 ---
The licensed driver had been driving comm ercial missions on line 082 between Ourense and Santiago 

--- Document Chunk 2079 ---
de Compostela from December 2011. He had completed a total of 59 missions in both directions, all

--- Document Chunk 2101 ---
3.2.3.3. Controls and internal audits 

--- Document Chunk 2102 ---
The description in this section relates to the bodies within Adif and Renfe Operadora which allow 

--- Document Chunk 2103 ---
participation with a view to improving traffic safety, in conformity to the corresponding Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2104 ---
Management System. This gives staff (crew, drivers, train managers etc.) a say in safety management. 

--- Document Chunk 2105 ---
The inspections carried out by both organisations on the Ourense - Santiago de Compostela lines have 

--- Document Chunk 2106 ---
therefore been reviewed within the purview of the accident zone.  

--- Document Chunk 2107 ---
3.2.3.3.1. Safety management participation bodies at Adif; review of their minutes  

--- Document Chunk 2108 ---
A) Participation bodies 

--- Document Chunk 2109 ---
Procedure SGSC/OPG, of 2009, governs bodies for participation in traffic safety management. In the 

--- Document Chunk 2110 ---
wake of organisational changes, there are now three committees: the General Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2111 ---
Committee; the Regional Traffic Safety Committee; and the Sectoral Technical Committee.  

--- Document Chunk 2112 ---
All are made up of staff  members of the various Adif directorates and areas answerable to the Traffic 

--- Document Chunk 2113 ---
Safety Directorate (various managerial tiers, depending on the committ ee in question). There are also 

--- Document Chunk 2114 ---
trade union representatives from the Company-Wide Works Council. 

--- Document Chunk 2115 ---
 The General Traffic Safety Committee  covers the whole scope of the network. It meets four 

--- Document Chunk 2116 ---
times a year, and its duties include: 

--- Document Chunk 2117 ---
 analysis and pooling of matters of general interest relating to traffic safety; and 

--- Document Chunk 2118 ---
 resolving both on matters raised by the other committees and on those raised by its own 

--- Document Chunk 2119 ---
members. 

--- Document Chunk 2120 ---
 There are three Sectoral Traffic Safety Technical Committees:  one for each of the following 

--- Document Chunk 2121 ---
fields: Conven tional Network Operations and Engineering; High -Speed Network Operations and 

--- Document Chunk 2122 ---
Engineering; and Logistical Services. The working scope of each committee is that of the 

--- Document Chunk 2123 ---
operations and action of the directorates represented on each committee. Ordinarily they m eet 

--- Document Chunk 2124 ---
three times a year and their duties include: 

--- Document Chunk 2125 ---
 studying detected traffic safety risks and proposing remedial measures;  

--- Document Chunk 2126 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2127 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2128 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2129 ---
A

 resolving on motions brought by their members and referring any matters relating to traffic
