3.2.3.3.2. Safety management participation bodies at Renfe Operadora and review of their minutes  

--- Document Chunk 2186 ---
A) Participation bodies 

--- Document Chunk 2187 ---
These bodies are governed by Procedure S MS-MN-A01: Organs of Governance of traffic SM S. There 

--- Document Chunk 2188 ---
are four traffic safety committees: the Central Committee; the Regional Committee; the Passenger 

--- Document Chunk 2189 ---
Area Operational Committee; and the Freight Area Operating Committee. 

--- Document Chunk 2190 ---
They consist of staff from the various directorates and areas of Renfe Operadora  answerable to the 

--- Document Chunk 2191 ---
Traffic Safety Directorate (at various managerial levels according to the committee in question). There 

--- Document Chunk 2192 ---
are also trade union delegates appointed by the Company -Wide Works Council. This ensures active 

--- Document Chunk 2193 ---
participation by all operating staff. 

--- Document Chunk 2194 ---
 The Central Traffic Safety Committee  is competent for the whole organisation. It holds four 

--- Document Chunk 2195 ---
ordinary meetings per year, and two extraordinary meetings (on specific topics). Its duties include 

--- Document Chunk 2196 ---
analysis and resolution on:  

--- Document Chunk 2197 ---
 matters raised by the Regional and Operational Committees; and 

--- Document Chunk 2198 ---
 matters brought up by its own members. 

--- Document Chunk 2199 ---
 There are two Operational Traffic Safety Committees : one for the Passenger Area and the 

--- Document Chunk 2200 ---
other for Freight and Logistics. Its scope is limited to operations. It meets four times a year, and  its 

--- Document Chunk 2201 ---
duties include:  

--- Document Chunk 2202 ---
 agreeing topics for referral to the Central Traffic Safety Committee and checking 

--- Document Chunk 2203 ---
implementation of resolutions passed by that Committee; 

--- Document Chunk 2204 ---
 analysis and resolution on matters raised by their own members; and 

--- Document Chunk 2205 ---
 following up the matters ref erred to the Central and/or Operational Committees until they are 

--- Document Chunk 2206 ---
finally closed. 

--- Document Chunk 2207 ---
 There are six Regional Traffic Safety Committees , one for each region of the Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2208 ---
Directorate. Their scope is limited to issues within their regions. The hold four ordinary meetings 

--- Document Chunk 2209 ---
per year and their duties include: 

--- Document Chunk 2210 ---
 monitoring the solution of defects detected on safety visits and inspections, within the scope 

--- Document Chunk 2211 ---
of their responsibility; 

--- Document Chunk 2212 ---
 resolving on matters referred to it or raised by their members;  

--- Document Chunk 2213 ---
 agreeing on matter s for referral to or processing in the Central Traffic Safety Committee and 

--- Document Chunk 2214 ---
checking implementation of the resolutions adopted by that Committee; and 

--- Document Chunk 2215 ---

3.2.3.3.3. Inspections by Adif 

--- Document Chunk 2250 ---
Adif’s Traffic Safety Directorate sets a number of in -cab inspections of traffic safety during journeys in 

--- Document Chunk 2251 ---
each region. These are specified in the Annual Traffic Safety Plan (PASC). 

--- Document Chunk 2252 ---
Procedure SGSC/ICC entails inspection in the ca b of conditions of travel during journeys. The purpose 

--- Document Chunk 2253 ---
is to check, from the driver’s cab, compliance with the regulations for driving staff and crew, 

--- Document Chunk 2254 ---
maintenance of the railway infrastructure and facilities necessary for operation, safety devices and 

--- Document Chunk 2255 ---
appliances in service, fitness to run, and the deployment of the necessary staff. 

--- Document Chunk 2256 ---

--- Document Chunk 2257 ---
Ourense and Santiago de Compostela: five in 2012 and three in 2013. One of  these took place on a 

--- Document Chunk 2258 ---
150/151 train service (Class 730). Another detected the only defect (repeated defects of the inspected 

--- Document Chunk 2259 ---
rolling stock). In all these cases, the driver’s behaviour was correct and professional. In no case were 

--- Document Chunk 2260 ---
defects of infrastructure or other incidents detected.

3.2.3.3.4. Inspections by Renfe Operadora 

--- Document Chunk 2277 ---
Renfe Operadora establishes an annual programme of accompanied train journeys, as part of the 

--- Document Chunk 2278 ---
Annual Action Programme of the Annual Safety Plan. It sets a minimum number of checks of this type 

--- Document Chunk 2279 ---
to carry out. For this purpose it provides Procedure SMS-PE-PCIA-01: Accompanied Train Journeys. 

--- Document Chunk 2280 ---
The aims of these checks are as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 2281 ---
 to check compliance with the regulations in force; 

--- Document Chunk 2282 ---
 to detect incorrect or incomplete practices by driving staff;  

--- Document Chunk 2283 ---
 to check correct fitting of safety devices on power cars;  

--- Document Chunk 2284 ---
 during the accompanied journey, to observe the condition of the infrastructure and signalling 

--- Document Chunk 2285 ---
equipment which may affect traffic safety; 

--- Document Chunk 2286 ---
 to observe staff behaviour and psychological and physical conditions which may affect them; 

--- Document Chunk 2287 ---
and 

--- Document Chunk 2288 ---
 to check the ergonomics of the vehicle and installations.  

--- Document Chunk 2289 ---
The methods of inspection include checking train safety logs. Hence Procedure S MS-PE-PCIA-04 

--- Document Chunk 2290 ---
governs management of safety recorder content. 

--- Document Chunk 2291 ---
Thus personnel of Renfe Operadora’s León Regional Delegation of the Traffic Safety Directorate and 

--- Document Chunk 2292 ---
of North Galicia Passenger Market Management were accompanied on journeys and their records 

--- Document Chunk 2293 ---
were ana lysed. In the period from 10  December 2011 to 24  July 2013, on the Ourense -Santiago 

--- Document Chunk 2294 ---
route, a total of 16 safety logs were analysed (equivalent to  1 411 km). 92 medium -distance train 

--- Document Chunk 2295 ---
journeys were accompanied (equivalent to 8  114 km), and another 35  long-distance (equivalent to 

--- Document Chunk 2296 ---
3 087 km). 

--- Document Chunk 2297 ---
According to certificates produced by these two departments, the inspections accomplished during the 

--- Document Chunk 2298 ---
stated period found no defect on the permanent way between Ourense and Santiago de Compostela 

--- Document Chunk 2299 ---
stations, on the 10 km up to the point of the derailment. 

--- Document Chunk 2300 ---
Annex 3.2.3.3.4 reproduces those Renfe Operadora certificates.

--- Document Chunk 2302 ---
The Accident & Incident Report (PAI) is a form for notifying occurrences during railway operations. 

--- Document Chunk 2303 ---
It has been in use since before separation of the now defunct RENFE.

Page 54 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 2318 ---
Renfe Operadora driving staff use form PAI to explain an occurrence or report defects which might 

--- Document Chunk 2319 ---
affect safety, and other business-related faults. The form includes details to identify where the  incident 

--- Document Chunk 2320 ---
occurred (train no, line, kilometre point etc.), description of the facts, measures adopted etc.  

--- Document Chunk 2321 ---
The Renfe Operadora Safety Management System includes the General Defect Management Procedure 

--- Document Chunk 2322 ---
(SMS-PG-16), which deals with defects forwarded by oper ating staff, on PAIs, as one of the channels 

--- Document Chunk 2323 ---
of communication of defects. The other channels it lists are: inspections; rolling stock defect logs; and 

--- Document Chunk 2324 ---
notifications by external personnel to the company. 

--- Document Chunk 2325 ---
Form PAI is normally in paper form. It is passed to t he driver’s next in line, who processes it and 

--- Document Chunk 2326 ---
forwards it for action, depending on the type of incident. Nevertheless, to help to make the 

--- Document Chunk 2327 ---
information in the PAIs known as quickly as possible, a computer application has recently been 

--- Document Chunk 2328 ---
developed. This makes it possible to e-mail the PAI to various addressees (not only the next in line).   

--- Document Chunk 2329 ---
Accordingly, CIAF investigators reviewed the PAIs in both paper and electronic format, originating from 

--- Document Chunk 2330 ---
the North  West Management and collected by the León Regional Delegat ion of the Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2331 ---
Directorate. They also reviewed reports made by other personnel and forwarded to that centre by 

--- Document Chunk 2332 ---
other means (memoranda, e-mails, telephone calls etc).  

--- Document Chunk 2333 ---
They reviewed a total of 21 reports, 4 of which were by PAI, for the whole of 2011. They reviewed 16 

--- Document Chunk 2334 ---
from 2012, of which 8 were PAIs. Up to 24 July 2013 (the date of the accident), there had been 

--- Document Chunk 2335 ---
17 reports, 10 of them by PAI. 

--- Document Chunk 2336 ---
The review carried out detected no incident at all relating to line 082 and therefore to the context of 

--- Document Chunk 2337 ---
the accident. 

--- Document Chunk 2338 ---
Thus Annex 3.2.3.3.5 contains a document from the León Regional Delegation of the Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2339 ---
Directorate certifying that the PAIs contain no mention of any incident on the section of track where 

--- Document Chunk 2340 ---
the derailment occurred, or on the 10 km leading to it.

So, as far as JM1’s comments made in his document are concerned, the problem posed by the 

--- Document Chunk 2466 ---
defective changeover from ERTMS to ASFA in the Santiago -bound direction (between PKs 77 and 80 ) 

--- Document Chunk 2467 ---
before the Angrois bend was passed on to Adif. The problem was solved by setting up temporary 

--- Document Chunk 2468 ---

--- Document Chunk 2469 ---
operation of the Class 121 rolling stock.  There is no record th at JM1’s second comment was passed 

--- Document Chunk 2470 ---
on to Adif: his warning of the danger of the curve itself.  

--- Document Chunk 2471 ---
On the other hand, as commented in previous sections (3.2.3.3.2), the Renfe Operadora SMS does 

--- Document Chunk 2472 ---
include organs for participation in safety management. Among these  are the six Regional Traffic 

--- Document Chunk 2473 ---
Safety Committees (CTSCs) - one for each region. One of these is León regional CTSC, which includes 

--- Document Chunk 2474 ---
the area of the North East Management (including Galicia).  

--- Document Chunk 2475 ---
As it happens, JP1 and his subordinate JM1 attended the meetings o f that Regional Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 2476 ---
Committee. Information about this was requested from Renfe Operadora. JM1 attended 36 of the 43 

--- Document Chunk 2477 ---
meetings of that committee from 2005. He attended all but one of the meetings held in 2011, 201 2 

--- Document Chunk 2478 ---
and 2013 (he was absent on 15 April 2011).  

--- Document Chunk 2479 ---
To sum up, with regard to JM1’s second comment, warning of the danger of the Angrois bend, at least 

--- Document Chunk 2480 ---
nine members of Renfe Operadora were in a position to know about this. It was not dealt with either at 

--- Document Chunk 2481 ---
the meetings monitoring the operation of Class 121 rolling stock, or a t the meetings of the Regional 

--- Document Chunk 2482 ---
Traffic Safety Committees (or in the other safety committees: the Central Committee and the Passenger 

--- Document Chunk 2483 ---
Operational Committee). JM1 attended those meetings. There is no record, either, of the warning being 

--- Document Chunk 2484 ---
passed on to Adif.

3.4. FUNCTIONING OF THE TECHNICAL INSTALLATIONS AND RAILWAY ROLLING STOCK  

--- Document Chunk 2582 ---
3.4.1. Control, Command and Signalling system 

--- Document Chunk 2583 ---
The context of the accident begins at signal E7 at the entry to A Grandeira branch. As stated in Notice 

--- Document Chunk 2584 ---
74 by Adif DSC, it falls within the electronic interlocking system of Santi ago de Compostela, which is 

--- Document Chunk 2585 ---
governed by Instruction Series A no 2556, of 16 July 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 2586 ---
This interlocking system can be managed by central control from Ourense Control Post and in local 

--- Document Chunk 2587 ---
control from Santiago de Compostela station. At the time of the accident, it was under local control. 

--- Document Chunk 2588 ---
So, in order to find out what indications the track signals were giving in the immediate run -up to the 

--- Document Chunk 2589 ---
accident, Adif and Renfe Operadora staff compiled an extract from the interlocking records, in the 

--- Document Chunk 2590 ---
presence of CIAF investigators. 

--- Document Chunk 2591 ---
With the cooperation of the provider of this technological installation (Dimetronic), the consistency of 

--- Document Chunk 2592 ---
the recorded data has been checked against the sequence of events on the video footage during the 

--- Document Chunk 2593 ---
time, and within the area, of the accident. 

--- Document Chunk 2594 ---
The interlocking events have been compiled from 20:40:00 to 20:43:39 hours on 24 July 2013. Attention 

--- Document Chunk 2595 ---
is drawn to the time mismatch between the train’s safety recorder (which is taken as a reference) and 

--- Document Chunk 2596 ---
the recorder of interlocking events. This mismatch a mounts to 2 minutes 32 seconds (the derailment 

--- Document Chunk 2597 ---
occurred at 20:41:06 hours on the train’s safety recorder and at interlocking time 20:43:38). 

--- Document Chunk 2598 ---
Analysis of the interlocking records against the video, from which photographs are attached, proves that 

--- Document Chunk 2599 ---
the path set for train 150/151 was, at all times, up to signal E8 at the entry to Santiago de Compostela 

--- Document Chunk 2600 ---
station on track 1. 

--- Document Chunk 2601 ---
Therefore the caution signal and the entry signal (E´7 and E7 respectively) for A Grandeira branch 

--- Document Chunk 2602 ---
were showing ‘track clear’ (green). The ne xt signal E’8, a caution signal for entry to Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 2603 ---
Compostela was showing ‘stop’ (yellow); while entry signal E8 at Santiago was showing ‘stop’ (red).

3.4.2. Infrastructure 

--- Document Chunk 2770 ---
3.4.2.1. Background 

--- Document Chunk 2771 ---
Information study 

--- Document Chunk 2772 ---
The Directorate -General of Railways of the Ministry of Development launched the Information Study 

--- Document Chunk 2773 ---
for the Project to Provide R ailway Access to Galicia, Ourense - Santiago Leg in December  1999. It 

--- Document Chunk 2774 ---
considered five alternative routes, with the same solution for access to Santiago de Compostela.  

--- Document Chunk 2775 ---
This underwent the official public in formation procedure in November  2001. 310 written su bmissions 

--- Document Chunk 2776 ---
were received, and the Information Study was altered as appropriate. None of the submissions raised 

--- Document Chunk 2777 ---
objections to the route in the accident zone. 

--- Document Chunk 2778 ---
In May 2002 the file was submitted to the Ministry of the Environment for the requisite environmenta l 

--- Document Chunk 2779 ---
impact declaration, which was given in March 2003. 

--- Document Chunk 2780 ---
The State Secretariat of Infrastructure at the Ministry of Development finally approved this Information 

--- Document Chunk 2781 ---
Study in April 2003. It opted to go ahead with alternative Solution C, with the modifications cont ained 

--- Document Chunk 2782 ---
in the public information file and in the environmental impact declaration. 

--- Document Chunk 2783 ---
Projects 

--- Document Chunk 2784 ---
By resolution of 30  April 2002, the State Secretariat of Infrastructure at the Ministry of Development 

--- Document Chunk 2785 ---
ordered the former Railway Infrastructure Manager  to draft the corresponding projects. It divided the 

--- Document Chunk 2786 ---
line into two sections (Ourense -Lalín and Lalín -Santiago) and began formalities to draw up the basic 

--- Document Chunk 2787 ---
projects in April 2003. It did not deal with access to Santiago and Ourense. 

--- Document Chunk 2788 ---
These two basic projects served for th e tendering in the competitive procedure for the design and 

--- Document Chunk 2789 ---
building of the track formation of the line. For this purpose, each of these two sections was initially 

--- Document Chunk 2790 ---
divided into six subsections (making a total of 12). These were put out to tender in April  2003. The 

--- Document Chunk 2791 ---
construction projects were drawn up and approved between June 2005 and April 2006. 

--- Document Chunk 2792 ---
For access to Santiago station (track formation), tenders were invited for a basic project in March  2006 

--- Document Chunk 2793 ---
and the construction project in April  2008. For access to O urense station (track formation), tenders 

--- Document Chunk 2794 ---
were invited for a basic project in August 2005 and the construction project in November 2008. 

--- Document Chunk 2795 ---
Bidding also proceeded for the construction projects f or the track assembly (November  2008), 

--- Document Chunk 2796 ---
electrification (July  2008) and install ations (September  2009) for the whole line. The tender was 

--- Document Chunk 2797 ---
subsequently drawn up. 

--- Document Chunk 2798 ---
This line was designed with track of the standard (UIC) gauge. Two gauge changers were installed: 

--- Document Chunk 2799 ---
one at Ourense (on the Santiago side, at PK 1+700 of line 082) and the other at Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 2800 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2801 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2802 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2803 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 2804 ---
MINISTRY OF 

--- Document Chunk 2805 ---
DEVELOPMENT  

--- Document Chunk 2806 ---
SUBSECRETARIAT 

--- Document Chunk 2807 ---
Investigation of Serious Accident 

--- Document Chunk 2808 ---
No 0054/2013, of 24.07.2013 

--- Document Chunk 2809 ---
Final Report RAILWAY ACCIDENTS 

--- Document Chunk 2810 ---
INVESTIGATION COMMISSION 

--- Document Chunk 2811 ---
ERA-2014-0070-00-00-ESEN 

--- Document Chunk 2812 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2813 ---
Page 66 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 2814 ---
Compostela station itself (on the A Coruña side). The aim was to connect the line to the rest of the rail 

--- Document Chunk 2815 ---
network on the Iberian gauge. 

--- Document Chunk 2816 ---
Consideration was also given to installing ERTMS between these two gauge changers. This sys tem 

--- Document Chunk 2817 ---
therefore extended to Santiago de Compostela station, although it only covered the new tracks laid 

--- Document Chunk 2818 ---
out. 

--- Document Chunk 2819 ---
This means that the standard gauge tracks planned between the Ourense gauge changer and that at 

--- Document Chunk 2820 ---
Santiago de Compostela station are governed by ERTMS  from CRC at Madrid -Atocha, whereas the 

--- Document Chunk 2821 ---
other tracks continue to be managed via the various interlocking systems (from Ourense and Santiago) 

--- Document Chunk 2822 ---
which incorporate ASFA. 

--- Document Chunk 2823 ---
The changeovers between the ERTMS installed on the new, standard -gauge tracks and the ASFA 

--- Document Chunk 2824 ---
system present on the conventional gauge tracks at Ourense and Santiago de Compostela stations 

--- Document Chunk 2825 ---
were planned at these gauge changers, using the manoeuvres to change the gauges of the trains.  

--- Document Chunk 2826 ---
Construction works 

--- Document Chunk 2827 ---
The contract for the track formation works on the Ourense-Santiago leg, on the section giving access to 

--- Document Chunk 2828 ---
Santiago de Compostela station, was awarded in July  2009. The works were completed in 

--- Document Chunk 2829 ---
November 2011. 

--- Document Chunk 2830 ---
The contract for assembly of the track on the section from O´Irixo to Santiago de Compostela was 

--- Document Chunk 2831 ---
awarded in May 2010 and the contract for the works of electrification between Ourense and Santiago 

--- Document Chunk 2832 ---
(the whole line) was awarded in February 2010. 

--- Document Chunk 2833 ---
The contract for the works on the safety and communications facilities (signalling, centralised traffic 

--- Document Chunk 2834 ---
control etc.) between Ourense an d Santiago was awarded in April  2010 and for the civil defence and 

--- Document Chunk 2835 ---
tunnel safety installations in April  2011. 

--- Document Chunk 2836 ---
The line commenced service in December 2011. 

--- Document Chunk 2837 ---
Modification of the original solution 

--- Document Chunk 2838 ---
During the course of the works, it was decided to make a modification. This was to provide Iberian track 

--- Document Chunk 2839 ---
gauge (rather than standard) throughout the line. This ensured continuity of the Iberian gauge 

--- Document Chunk 2840 ---
throughout the Galician rail network. The originally planned gauge changers were cancelled, because two 

--- Document Chunk 2841 ---
gauge changeovers in just 90 km would seriously erode the time savings achieved by the new section. In 

--- Document Chunk 2842 ---
future, when standard gauge might be available on other, basically southward, stretches, the switch 

--- Document Chunk 2843 ---
would be made to this gauge with multi-purpose sleepers available. 

--- Document Chunk 2844 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2845 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2846 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2847 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 2848 ---
MINISTRY OF 

--- Document Chunk 2849 ---
DEVELOPMENT  

--- Document Chunk 2850 ---

--- Document Chunk 2851 ---
Investigation of Serious Accident 

--- Document Chunk 2852 ---
No 0054/2013, of 24.07.2013 

--- Document Chunk 2853 ---
Final Report RAILWAY ACCIDENTS 

--- Document Chunk 2854 ---
INVESTIGATION COMMISSION 

--- Document Chunk 2855 ---
ERA-2014-0070-00-00-ESEN 

--- Document Chunk 2856 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2857 ---
Page 67 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 2858 ---
The change of gauge, from standard to Iberian, also made it possible to increase the functionality of the 

--- Document Chunk 2859 ---
new line (082). It no longer entered single track at Santiago. Instead, connection was possible with the 

--- Document Chunk 2860 ---
Eje Atlántico toward s Vigo (line 824) without the need for manoeuvres at Santiago de Compostela 

--- Document Chunk 2861 ---
station. However, the A Grandeira and Río Sar (line 842) branches had to be available for this purpose. 

--- Document Chunk 2862 ---
Thus, in June  2010, the initially planned solution was reconsidered. A propo sal was made in 

--- Document Chunk 2863 ---
October 2010 to modify it. The Ministry of Development authorised this in April 2011. 

--- Document Chunk 2864 ---
This decision necessitated a change of plan, mainly to the safety and communication installations 

--- Document Chunk 2865 ---
(ERTMS and ASFA location), track assembly (sleepers and track gear) and electrification (catenary). 

--- Document Chunk 2866 ---
As regards the signalling and control installations, given that the new gauge allowed movements 

--- Document Chunk 2867 ---
to/from other existing lines managed by the Santiago interlocking system, it was arranged that this 

--- Document Chunk 2868 ---
interlocking sys tem would also manage the section of this new line where it accessed Santiago de 

--- Document Chunk 2869 ---
Compostela, plus the A Grandeira and Río Sar branches. As commented, this access section had ASFA, 

--- Document Chunk 2870 ---
not ERTMS.  

--- Document Chunk 2871 ---
It was therefore necessary to set the new boundaries of manageme nt of the interlocking system of 

--- Document Chunk 2872 ---
Santiago de Compostela station (and the boundaries at Ourense). This would now include governance 

--- Document Chunk 2873 ---
of the access sections to the new line and its interconnections with the existing tracks. 

--- Document Chunk 2874 ---
Further thought then had to be give n to the locations of the changeovers between the ERTMS safety 

--- Document Chunk 2875 ---
system planned on the new line and the ASFA system on the conventional rail network. So far these 

--- Document Chunk 2876 ---
changeovers had been provided at the planned gauge changeovers. Now, the new boundaries were 

--- Document Chunk 2877 ---
set between both systems on the new build line (082). 

--- Document Chunk 2878 ---
These changeovers must comply with the Adif standard ‘Functional Requirements and Engineering 

--- Document Chunk 2879 ---
Rules for ERTMS L1 and L2. Version 2.4.0 dated 22/10/2009 ’. More specifically, section 5.2.6 

--- Document Chunk 2880 ---
‘Changeover from ERTMS/ETCS Level 1 to ASFA ’ states that changeovers to ASFA must be announced 

--- Document Chunk 2881 ---
and arranged on the route, and always before a caution signal. 

--- Document Chunk 2882 ---
As the Santiago de Compostela interlocking system includes the bypass A Grandeira branch (and the 

--- Document Chunk 2883 ---
Río Sar branch), it was then necessary to position this changeover in the Ourense - Santiago direction 

--- Document Chunk 2884 ---
before the caution signals E´7 (for track 1) and E´9 (for track 2). Both of these are located at PK 

--- Document Chunk 2885 ---
80+619. Hence, in deference to the standard, the changeover was locate d at PK 80+06 9 (actual PK; 

--- Document Chunk 2886 ---
the PK 80+169 in the project). 

--- Document Chunk 2887 ---
The arrangements for changeover from ASFA to ERTMS are established in section 5.2.5: ‘Changeover 

--- Document Chunk 2888 ---
from ASFA to ERTMS/ETCS Level 1’ of the standard. It states that the order to change to level 1 must be 

--- Document Chunk 2889 ---
given in a group of fixed signal balises. Thus, in the opposite direction, Santiago - Ourense, on the 

--- Document Chunk 2890 ---
access tracks to Santiago the changeover was made at signals 844 (track 1) and 842 (track 2), the 

--- Document Chunk 2891 ---
first signals located after the bypass of A Grandeira branch, at PK 84+200.  

--- Document Chunk 2892 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2893 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2894 ---

On the access tracks to Ourense, the changeovers were made in  a similar way. In the 

--- Document Chunk 2907 ---

--- Document Chunk 2908 ---

--- Document Chunk 2909 ---

--- Document Chunk 2910 ---

--- Document Chunk 2911 ---
Changeovers from ERTMS to ASFA (and vice versa) also occur on other high -speed lines on the RFIG, 

--- Document Chunk 2912 ---
generally at access routes to stations. One example is Madrid -Atocha (access from the Madrid -

--- Document Chunk 2913 ---
Barcelona high-speed line), Málaga, Valladolid and Albacete. 

--- Document Chunk 2914 ---
It should be pointed out that the decision taken at the time, to modify the physical cover of the ERTMS, 

--- Document Chunk 2915 ---
has no direct bearing on the establishment of the specific causes of this accident, since the 

--- Document Chunk 2916 ---
circumstances of incompatibility, which obliged that train to travel on BSL and ASFA, might have occurred 

--- Document Chunk 2917 ---
just the same if the ERTMS had included Santiago de Compostela station. 

--- Document Chunk 2918 ---
Annex 3.4.2.1 contains a diagram of the originally planned tracks and those actually laid after the 

--- Document Chunk 2919 ---
approved modification.  

--- Document Chunk 2920 ---
3.4.2.2. Authorisation to commission line 082 

--- Document Chunk 2921 ---
Article 81h of Law  39/2003 on the Rail Sector lists, among the matters for whic h the Ministry of 

--- Document Chunk 2922 ---
Development is competent, the granting of certificates of opening of lines to public transport before 

--- Document Chunk 2923 ---
operation thereof commences. 

--- Document Chunk 2924 ---
Article 16 of the Regulation under the Rail Sector Law, passed by Royal Decree 2387/2004, develops 

--- Document Chunk 2925 ---
the above. It requires Ministry of Development authorisation to be held before commissioning a line on 

--- Document Chunk 2926 ---
the RFIG. This must state that it can be commissioned, provided that it meets the safety conditions 

--- Document Chunk 2927 ---
required by the applicable regulations.  

--- Document Chunk 2928 ---
The same Article add s that such authorisation must be granted by the Director -General of Railways, 

--- Document Chunk 2929 ---
having seen the following documentation: 

--- Document Chunk 2930 ---
 Report of conformity of the built structures to the technical regulations applicable, issued by 

--- Document Chunk 2931 ---
the personnel responsible for their construction and supervision; 

--- Document Chunk 2932 ---
 documentation received proving completed execution of the test plan established by the 

--- Document Chunk 2933 ---
infrastructure manager or, as applicable, the Directorate-General of Railways (DGF); and 

--- Document Chunk 2934 ---
 certification from the infrastructure manager (in this  case Adif) of fulfilment of the set 

--- Document Chunk 2935 ---
conditions concerning safe railway operation.  

--- Document Chunk 2936 ---
So, based on the above, Adif passed its application file to DGF for authorisation to commission the new 

--- Document Chunk 2937 ---
line 082, from Ourense (PK 0+000) to Santiago de Compostela (PK 88+241).  

--- Document Chunk 2938 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 2939 ---

3.4.2.2.1. Safety file 

--- Document Chunk 3146 ---
Issue of the safety certificate by Adif (which is necessary for the Ministry of Development/DGF to 

--- Document Chunk 3147 ---
authorise commissioning) is based, with reference to the Command/Control and Signa lling 

--- Document Chunk 3148 ---
subsystem (CMS), on the safety file in accordance with Adif’s internal procedures.  

--- Document Chunk 3149 ---
Thus Adif has a procedure ‘certification of fulfilment of applicable traffic safety conditions by the 

--- Document Chunk 3150 ---
Command/Control and Signalling subsystem,’ which forms part of its Safety Management System. 

--- Document Chunk 3151 ---
According to that procedure, the traffic safety certificate is based on the safety file. This file, which 

--- Document Chunk 3152 ---
concentrates on the Command/Control and Signalling subsystem, consists of documents demonstrating 

--- Document Chunk 3153 ---
the safety of the syste m installed on the track. The safety case and Independent Assessment Report 

--- Document Chunk 3154 ---
supplement this file. 

--- Document Chunk 3155 ---
Among the standards followed by these documents are CENELEC EN -50129 (and also EN -50126 and 

--- Document Chunk 3156 ---

(TSI) relating to the Command/Control and Signalling subsystem  dated 7 November 2006. This does 

--- Document Chunk 3158 ---
not apply to the existing subsystems and equipment.

3.4.2.3. Maintenance 

--- Document Chunk 3240 ---
Rail network maintenance operations include preventive maintenance, such as inspection and 

--- Document Chunk 3241 ---
monitoring of railway lines. With regard to monitoring, a distinction can be made between dynamic 

--- Document Chunk 3242 ---
monitoring, monitoring of track geometry, and other forms. Track monitoring relies on moving vehicles 

--- Document Chunk 3243 ---
which collect readings of various parameters for further processing and analysis. 

--- Document Chunk 3244 ---
Geometric monitoring takes place using specialist vehicles and generally takes place annually. It takes 

--- Document Chunk 3245 ---
direct readings of longitudinal level, transverse level (cant), warping, track gauge, plane line alignm ent 

--- Document Chunk 3246 ---
etc. There are three levels of analysis: I, II and III. Basically, level I records safety parameters; level II 

--- Document Chunk 3247 ---
ride comfort; and III track fatigue via the rail (vertical, lateral and rolling contact fatigue) and track 

--- Document Chunk 3248 ---
gauge.  

--- Document Chunk 3249 ---
Dynamic monitoring can be performed on specialist vehicles or on the rolling stock in service, at 

--- Document Chunk 3250 ---
operating speed. This generally takes place quarterly and is an indirect method of finding out the 

--- Document Chunk 3251 ---
condition of the track. It measures the accelerations to which the vehicle is exposed  in given zones, by 

--- Document Chunk 3252 ---
positioning accelerometers at strategic points. 

--- Document Chunk 3253 ---
Dynamic monitoring measures transverse (or lateral) acceleration on bogies (or wheelsets, as in this 

--- Document Chunk 3254 ---
case), which is associated with static or dynamic warping and misalignments with a shor t wavelength. 

--- Document Chunk 3255 ---
It also detects vertical acceleration on the axle box, which is associated with short -wave levelling 

--- Document Chunk 3256 ---
defects on each rail (welds, slipping etc.), and lateral and vertical acceleration on the vehicle shell 

--- Document Chunk 3257 ---
(body), which is associated with long -wave levelling defects and misalignment which affect passenger 

--- Document Chunk 3258 ---
comfort. Finally, it detects uncompensated lateral acceleration. 

--- Document Chunk 3259 ---
In the accident zone, the last geometric monitoring  (before the accident) took place on 

--- Document Chunk 3260 ---
21 November 2012. The readings for all parameters were good, except a small levelling defect (low 

--- Document Chunk 3261 ---
point) which could hardly be classed ‘ZUT’ (a zone requiring urgent attention).  

--- Document Chunk 3262 ---
This low point was located towards PK 84+245, at the start of the Angrois bend, and corresponded to 

--- Document Chunk 3263 ---
the transition wedge of the first pier of viaduct E -01 (in the direction of travel of the train involved in 

--- Document Chunk 3264 ---
the accident). It was repaired in December 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 3265 ---
The last dynamic monitoring took place on 8 May 2013. It used specialist vehicle BT-2, which confirmed 

--- Document Chunk 3266 ---
the good condition of the track. All the acceleration values measured on the vehicle were far from the 

--- Document Chunk 3267 ---
minimum monitoring thresholds and well in excess of the values for scheduled or urgent intervention. 

--- Document Chunk 3268 ---
Annex 3.4.2.3  contains the data from the geometric monitoring (a nalysis I) carried out in 

--- Document Chunk 3269 ---
November 2011 and the dynamic monitoring carried out in May 2012.  

--- Document Chunk 3270 ---

3.4.2.4. Measurement of track data  

--- Document Chunk 3301 ---
After the event, in the morning of 25  July 2013, safety technicians from Renfe Operadora and Adif, in 

--- Document Chunk 3302 ---
the presence of CIAF members, proceeded to measure various track parameters in the derailment 

--- Document Chunk 3303 ---
zone. 

--- Document Chunk 3304 ---
They measured the track from point 0 (beginni ng of derailment - PK 84+413) forwards for 15  m and 

--- Document Chunk 3305 ---
backwards for 35  m (normally this is only done for 15  m). They measured the values for track gauge 

--- Document Chunk 3306 ---
and cant, metre by metre. This interval also fell entirely within the transition curve (clothoid) leading  to 

--- Document Chunk 3307 ---
the 402 m circular curve (the Angrois bend). 

--- Document Chunk 3308 ---
Annex 3.4.2.4 contains the sheet of measured track data.  

--- Document Chunk 3309 ---
With regard to track gauge , the theoretical value is 1668 mm. Standard NAV 7.3.2.0 - Track 

--- Document Chunk 3310 ---
qualification:  track gauge sets maximum tolerances of -3 mm and +15  mm for the theoretical value 

--- Document Chunk 3311 ---
for curves of radius greater than or equal to 400  m. The measurement on location found values 

--- Document Chunk 3312 ---
ranging from -0.1 to +0.9 mm in the 15 m after point 0. On the 35  m before, the values ranged from 

--- Document Chunk 3313 ---
0 to +2.3 mm. The track gauge values were therefore within tolerance. 

--- Document Chunk 3314 ---
For track gauge variation, the same standard allows a tolerance of 2  mm between successive sleepers. 

--- Document Chunk 3315 ---
This implies 3.33  mm/m (for speeds greater than 60  km/h). Here, the maximum variations measured 

--- Document Chunk 3316 ---
were 1 mm (between points +9 and +10) and 1.6  mm (between points -29 and -30), relating to the 

--- Document Chunk 3317 ---
sections before and after point 0 respectively. Hence the readings for gauge variation were within 

--- Document Chunk 3318 ---
tolerance.

--- Document Chunk 3339 ---

--- Document Chunk 3340 ---

--- Document Chunk 3341 ---

--- Document Chunk 3342 ---

--- Document Chunk 3344 ---

3.4.2.5. Verification of maximum permitted speed admissible on Angrois bend and 

--- Document Chunk 3349 ---
fixed signalling in the zone 

--- Document Chunk 3350 ---
A plane survey was carried out on location on the Angrois bend. This confirmed its layout parameters. After 

--- Document Chunk 3351 ---
a straight section, the curve begins at PK 84+228. A first section of curve represents a 200 m transition, in 

--- Document Chunk 3352 ---
the form of a clothoid where parameter A = 283.8. This ends at PK 84+428, the start of the circular curve 

--- Document Chunk 3353 ---
402 m in radius and 265 m in length. This ends at PK 84+693, where another transition section, similar to 

--- Document Chunk 3354 ---
the first, begins. This is 200 m in length and has a clothoid of parameter A = 283.8 ending at PK 84+893, 

--- Document Chunk 3355 ---
where a straight begins. 

--- Document Chunk 3356 ---
The curve has a 130  mm cant, so that the variation in the transition zones i s 0.65 mm/m. Both values 

--- Document Chunk 3357 ---
are normal. As there is an 80  km/h speed limit on the curve, the unbalanced acceleration (Asc) 

--- Document Chunk 3358 ---
obtained for that speed is 0.50  m/s2, below the normally established value for type N (normal) trains, 

--- Document Chunk 3359 ---
which is 0.65 m/s2. The latter value would be reached at a speed of 85 km/h. 

--- Document Chunk 3360 ---
Considering the 8 mm cant deficiency found by the measurement on location in the transition zone (in 

--- Document Chunk 3361 ---
the immediate vicinity of point 0), the actual cant on the curve would be 122  mm (theoretical: 

--- Document Chunk 3362 ---
130 mm), giving rise to an unbalanced acceleration of 0.54 m/s 2. That value is still below the 

--- Document Chunk 3363 ---
permitted maximum (0.65 m/s2). 

--- Document Chunk 3364 ---
Nevertheless, the dynamic monitoring commented on in a previous section took place at 72 km/h while 

--- Document Chunk 3365 ---
taking the Angrois bend. It resulted in an unb alanced acceleration of 0.26  m/s2, consistent with the 

--- Document Chunk 3366 ---
presence of an actual cant of 130 mm.

With regard to signalling, on the other hand, there is a series of sign boards in the Santiago -Ourense 

--- Document Chunk 3385 ---
direction on li ne 082. These run from the end of the ERTMS (PK 80+069) to point 0 (PK 84+413) of 

--- Document Chunk 3386 ---

--- Document Chunk 3388 ---
 Board marked ‘change ASFA mode’ at PK 80+803 

--- Document Chunk 3389 ---

--- Document Chunk 3390 ---
the new line 082 and other lines affected. It specifies that this signal must be set up for trains running 

--- Document Chunk 3391 ---
to and from line 082 with ASFA equipment connected. It indicates the point where the change of mode 

--- Document Chunk 3392 ---
must take place (from high-speed to conventional ASFA - as in this case - or vice versa).  

--- Document Chunk 3393 ---
Taking into account that the ERTMS finishes at PK 80+069 (and theref ore also the high-speed back-up 

--- Document Chunk 3394 ---
ASFA), the sign board indicating the changeover is further on (at PK 80+803). 

--- Document Chunk 3395 ---
 Board marked ‘RGC’ at PK 84+176 (post of entry signal E7) 

--- Document Chunk 3396 ---

--- Document Chunk 3397 ---
of the regulations : General Traffic Regulation (RGC) or Technical and Operating Requirements for 

--- Document Chunk 3398 ---
Traffic and Safety (PTOs). It must be set up near the signals delimiting the areas covered (by the RGC 

--- Document Chunk 3399 ---
or PTO). 

--- Document Chunk 3400 ---
Notice 74 adds that the PTOs apply from Coto da Torre branch to A Grandeira branch (PK 85.0). That 

--- Document Chunk 3401 ---
is why the ‘RGC’ board is positioned at PK 84+176, to indicate that the train is about to enter this area 

--- Document Chunk 3402 ---
(from PK 85.0). 

--- Document Chunk 3403 ---
 Fixed sign to reduce speed at PK 84+273 

--- Document Chunk 3404 ---
As PTO Article 217 states: ‘change of maximum speed’, this sign marks the point on the line where the 

--- Document Chunk 3405 ---
maximum speed permitted for the infrastructure changes, as per the Maximum Speed Tables. The 

--- Document Chunk 3406 ---
kilometre point on the line is written on the inside of the sign (in orange when the change is to a lower 

--- Document Chunk 3407 ---
speed, and in blue when it is to a higher speed). This is the point from which the new maximum speed 

--- Document Chunk 3408 ---
must be complied with. The sign is positioned 100 metres along the line where the change of speed 

--- Document Chunk 3409 ---
occurs. 

--- Document Chunk 3410 ---
According to the Speed Table for line 082, it is compulsory to slow to 80 km/h at PK 84+230 (the Angrois 

--- Document Chunk 3411 ---
bend). Hence this sign is located within the corresponding 100 -metre length (at PK 84+273) and is 

--- Document Chunk 3412 ---
orange (because it marks a reduction). It is marked ‘84.2’.

3.4.3. Rolling stock 

--- Document Chunk 3429 ---
The 730.012 unit involved in the accident is the result of a modification of the 130.012, to allow it to 

--- Document Chunk 3430 ---
run on unelectrified lines. Basically, therefore,  the end passenger coaches ( Nos 2 and 12) were 

--- Document Chunk 3431 ---
modified, and converted into end diesel generator cars (‘CET’ vehicles). 

--- Document Chunk 3432 ---
CETs incorporate the diesel generation plant and auxiliary installations necessary to operate 

--- Document Chunk 3433 ---
themselves (refrigeration, diesel fuel supply, air intake and silencer) and to supply electricity to the 

--- Document Chunk 3434 ---
motors. 

--- Document Chunk 3435 ---
To function in diesel-electric mode, Class 730 trains are equipped with a 1800 kW diesel engine and a 

--- Document Chunk 3436 ---
1600-litre diesel fuel tank which supplies it. There is one of these in each of the two CET cars.  

--- Document Chunk 3437 ---
Because of the weight of the diesel generation plant, the CET car has a towed bogie at the end and 

--- Document Chunk 3438 ---
shares a wheelset with the adjacent coach. Logically, both are of variable gauge. The bogie was 

--- Document Chunk 3439 ---
developed from the Class 130. 

--- Document Chunk 3440 ---
Annex 3.4.3 shows a general diagram of the Class 730 and a detail of a CET generator car. 

--- Document Chunk 3441 ---
3.4.3.1. Authorisations 

--- Document Chunk 3442 ---
The regulation governing conditions of railway rolling stock approval is Order FOM/233/2006, of 

--- Document Chunk 3443 ---
31 January 2006. In this case, it is supplemented by Circular Resolution 10/2008 on the validation 

--- Document Chunk 3444 ---
procedure in cases of applications for author isation to commission modified rolling stock, which 

--- Document Chunk 3445 ---
develops this aspect and makes it more specific. 

--- Document Chunk 3446 ---
Therefore, based on the above -mentioned regulations, the modified Class 730 rolling stock, like new 

--- Document Chunk 3447 ---
rolling stock, must have the mandatory authorisation of commissioning issued by the Directorate-General 

--- Document Chunk 3448 ---
of Railways, and the relevant authorisation to run, issued by the Adif Traffic Safety Directorate, since this 

--- Document Chunk 3449 ---
is a significant modification in the terms of Circular 10/2008. 

--- Document Chunk 3450 ---
Authorisation is granted for comm issioning once proof has been given of fulfilment of the 

--- Document Chunk 3451 ---
requirements, conditions and technical regulations applicable, and after an approval and test process. 

--- Document Chunk 3452 ---
Next, the authorisation for running certifies the vehicle’s compatibility with the infrastructur e and 

--- Document Chunk 3453 ---
specifies the conditions in which it may travel on the lines of the RFIG. 

--- Document Chunk 3454 ---
The 130.012 unit held a running authorisation dated 27  June 2008. The 730.012 unit had likewise 

--- Document Chunk 3455 ---
been granted authorisation for commissioning on 11  June 2012, and authorisation for running on 

--- Document Chunk 3456 ---
13 June 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 3457 ---
Annex 3.4.3.1 shows the documents which constitute evidence of these authorisations.

For the purpose of obtaining running authorisation from Adif, the order referred to above also requires 

--- Document Chunk 3474 ---
approval of the appropriate maintenance plan and the maintenance centres earmarked to carry out the 

--- Document Chunk 3475 ---
operations described in that plan. 

--- Document Chunk 3476 ---
The maintenance centres in turn must hold the appropriate approval issued by the Directorate -General 

--- Document Chunk 3477 ---
of Railways based on the company’s technical competence, personnel and finances. 

--- Document Chunk 3478 ---
The appropriate Adif approval must also be held for each type of maintenance work to be done, 

--- Document Chunk 3479 ---
depending on the features of the railway vehicle for maintenance. 

--- Document Chunk 3480 ---
Renfe Operadora is the body responsible for maintaining the Class 730 railcar units, which it owns. The 

--- Document Chunk 3481 ---
companies responsible for maintaining this rolling stock are Patentes Talgo, S.L., and Btren Mantenimiento 

--- Document Chunk 3482 ---
Ferroviario, S.A. (in which Renfe and Bombardier have participating interests). 

--- Document Chunk 3483 ---
Both companies hold the relevant approvals from the Directorate -General of Railways, granted on 

--- Document Chunk 3484 ---
19 November 2008 and 29 September 2011, respectively. 

--- Document Chunk 3485 ---
Talgo and Btren jointly maintain the Class 730 units at the workshop at the Fuencarral High -Speed 

--- Document Chunk 3486 ---
Maintenance Base, 28022 Madr id. For this purpose they hold the mandatory Adif authorisation, dated 

--- Document Chunk 3487 ---
13 June 2012 and valid for five years. This allows them to carry out operation types IS, IB, IM1, IM2, 

--- Document Chunk 3488 ---
IM3 and IM4, in increasing order of importance (see annexed table). 

--- Document Chunk 3489 ---
The maintenance plan is structured into intervals, depending on the number of kilometres travelled in 

--- Document Chunk 3490 ---
each case. Thus, when a given level of servicing is carried out, it includes all the operations of all the 

--- Document Chunk 3491 ---
lower levels of servicing. 

--- Document Chunk 3492 ---
In its original configuration as a  railcar, unit 130.012 was subject to Maintenance Plan code 

--- Document Chunk 3493 ---
PM.1300.10, edition 0 of which was dated 26 November 2007. Version 5 is currently in force.

plan, the following servicing was carried out:

3.4.3.5. Brake test 

--- Document Chunk 3726 ---
3.4.3.5.1. At Madrid-Chamartín and Ourense stations 

--- Document Chunk 3727 ---
As specified in Article 538 of the General Traffic Regulation, before allowing a train to depart from its station 

--- Document Chunk 3728 ---
of origin, or an intermediate station where its make -up has been altered, it is necessary t o carry out 

--- Document Chunk 3729 ---
operating tests on the brake, in accordance with the provision of this Regulation and of the Operating 

--- Document Chunk 3730 ---
Manual (Chapter 4: Brake Tests), in order to check that the braking of the trains is in working order. 

--- Document Chunk 3731 ---
Train 150/151 left Madrid in its direc tion of travel with 730  class rakes 013 and 012 coupled. At 

--- Document Chunk 3732 ---
Ourense they were separated. One went towards Pontevedra and Vigo (rake 013) and the other (rake 

--- Document Chunk 3733 ---
012, involved in the accident) headed for Santiago de Compostela, A Coruña and Ferrol.  

--- Document Chunk 3734 ---
The required brake tests were carried out on the train involved in the accident at Madrid -Chamartín, its 

--- Document Chunk 3735 ---
station of departure, and at Ourense, its intermediate stop. On this class of rolling stock, the brake test 

--- Document Chunk 3736 ---
is carried out automatically from the driver’s cab. The data are stored in the safety recorder. 

--- Document Chunk 3737 ---
 [In numbers] 

--- Document Chunk 3738 ---
.

--- Document Chunk 3769 ---
The data recorded at the brake test carried out at Madrid -Chamartín show that it was carried out at 

--- Document Chunk 3770 ---
around 14:30 hours, before the train departed, and that there was one axle with a brake overridden.  

--- Document Chunk 3771 ---
The train’s de parture was not conditional on this, as Adif Instruction C 25, of 13  June 2012, 

--- Document Chunk 3772 ---
establishes. This contains special requirements for running Class 730 and other locomotives on RFIG 

--- Document Chunk 3773 ---
lines. It allows a double rake to run with up to 12 axles with brake overrid den (six for a single rake), 

--- Document Chunk 3774 ---
although there is a speed limit. This does not apply if a brake is not available on just one axle.  

--- Document Chunk 3775 ---
After the two rakes (013 and 012) were uncoupled at Ourense, the brake tests of both were repeated. 

--- Document Chunk 3776 ---
According to the recorder for rake 013, the test took place at around 20:00 hours, before departure for 

--- Document Chunk 3777 ---
Pontevedra, and showed that one axle still had a brake overridden. Logically, this was the one 

--- Document Chunk 3778 ---
detected in Madrid. The recorder for rake 012 shows that the brake test was also car ried out at around 

--- Document Chunk 3779 ---
20:00 hours, and that it had brakes on all its axles. There was no sign of a brake overridden on any 

--- Document Chunk 3780 ---
axle. 

--- Document Chunk 3781 ---
Annex 3.4.3.5 contains the safety recorder data. It shows that one brake was unavailable on one 

--- Document Chunk 3782 ---
axle at Madrid and Ourense.  

--- Document Chunk 3783 ---
3.4.3.5.2. Brake check in situ 

--- Document Chunk 3784 ---
Train 150/151, consisting of rake 730.012, carr ied out emergency braking on 24  July 2013, near the 

--- Document Chunk 3785 ---
Angrois bend moments before the accident. The data from the safety recorder, located on power car 045, 

--- Document Chunk 3786 ---
which was running in position 1 as power car, show that this braking began by the driver operating the 

--- Document Chunk 3787 ---
service brake handle, by moving it to the emergency position (rapid braking).  

--- Document Chunk 3788 ---
According to information from Talgo (diagnosis), the figures obtained from the record of the train’s 

--- Document Chunk 3789 ---
technical parameters show that, at the time the emergency brake was applied, the train was moving at a 

--- Document Chunk 3790 ---
pre-set speed. Therefore, when it entered a 12.5‰ slope, traction did not apply and the electric brake was 

--- Document Chunk 3791 ---
applied lightly. This took place automatically, to counter the effects of the slope in order not to exceed the 

--- Document Chunk 3792 ---
pre-set speed. 

--- Document Chunk 3793 ---
On the section between the time of application of the emergency brake (PK 84+009) until the 

--- Document Chunk 3794 ---
derailment occurred (PK 84+413), the train’s braking curve has been compared with the following two 

--- Document Chunk 3795 ---
curves: braking curve under the conditions set by the Rolling Stock Technical Specification for 

--- Document Chunk 3796 ---
Interoperability (TSI) and the braking curve most similar to the actual curve from the tests carried out 

--- Document Chunk 3797 ---
during approval of the Class 730 rolling stock. 

--- Document Chunk 3798 ---
These two curves have been adjusted to the conditions under which rake 730.012 was running on the 

--- Document Chunk 3799 ---
day of the accident. This means they have been corrected to take account of wheel diameter, train 

--- Document Chunk 3800 ---
loading and longitudinal track profile (slope/incline). 

--- Document Chunk 3801 ---
It can be deduced from this comparison that the behaviour of rake 730.012 during the emergency 

--- Document Chunk 3802 ---
braking prior to the accident matches the description for braking curves in the TSI and in the approval 

--- Document Chunk 3803 ---
of the Class 730 rolling stock. Hence the braking performance was correct.

--- Document Chunk 3818 ---
On the other hand, based on the data gathered by the safety recorder in the power car, the value of 

--- Document Chunk 3819 ---
deceleration produced by the emergency braking near the Angrois bend can be estimated.  

--- Document Chunk 3820 ---
It is recorded that the emergency brake was applied at 2 0:40:59 hours while travelling at 195  km/h 

--- Document Chunk 3821 ---
(at PK 84+009). The system delayed three seconds before actually braking. Hence it was 20:41:02, 

--- Document Chunk 3822 ---
speed 195  km/h (at PK 84+171), when deceleration began. The train left the rails (point 0) at 

--- Document Chunk 3823 ---
20:41:06 (four seconds  later) while moving at 179  km/h (at PK 84+413).  

--- Document Chunk 3824 ---
In the four seconds of effective braking, a distance of 242  m was covered and the speed was 

--- Document Chunk 3825 ---
reduced by  16 km/h. This resulted in decele ration of 1.11 m/s2. This value, plus the equivalent three 

--- Document Chunk 3826 ---
seconds (delay in actual application of the brake), conform to the provisions of the Rolling Stock TSI 

--- Document Chunk 3827 ---
(decision 2008/232/EC, table 7, box A). This states that, for speeds between 230 and 170  km/h, the 

--- Document Chunk 3828 ---
minimum deceleration is 1.05 m/s2 and the time equivalent is three seconds. 

--- Document Chunk 3829 ---
3.4.3.6. Withdrawal of authorisation to run Class 730 rolling stock on ERTMS between 

--- Document Chunk 3830 ---
Ourense and Santiago de Compostela  

--- Document Chunk 3831 ---
To function correctly, a safety system, whether ASFA or ERTMS, must not only be correctly installed, 

--- Document Chunk 3832 ---
both on the track and in the train, but the versions must be mutually compatible. 

--- Document Chunk 3833 ---
Article 15 of Directive 2008/57 on the interoperability of the rail system within the Community 

--- Document Chunk 3834 ---
provides that the Member States shall authorise the placing in service of structural subsystems, 

--- Document Chunk 3835 ---
checking the te chnical compatibility of these subsystems with the system into which they are being 

--- Document Chunk 3836 ---
integrated. 

--- Document Chunk 3837 ---
With reference to the Command/Control and Signalling subsystem , Spain therefore carries out 

--- Document Chunk 3838 ---
‘integration tests’, previously called ‘supplementary tests ’, which seek to verify the technical 

--- Document Chunk 3839 ---
compatibility of the train with the network. This is not a validation either of track equipment or of the 

--- Document Chunk 3840 ---
train’s on-board equipment. 

--- Document Chunk 3841 ---
Thus the complementary tests of the Class 730 units on line 082 took place to analyse the tra in-track 

--- Document Chunk 3842 ---
integration of the ERTMS L1. They were carried out in February 2012 on different parts of line 082. 

--- Document Chunk 3843 ---
More specifically, the tests relating to the changeover from level STM EBICAB (with ASFA functionality) to 

--- Document Chunk 3844 ---
ERTMS L1 took place on track 2, towards Ourense, at the first group of balises on the Santiago side. 

--- Document Chunk 3845 ---
Commercial service on the new line 082 between Ourense and Santiago de Compostela began on 

--- Document Chunk 3846 ---
10 December 2011. Initially the Madrid -A Coruña link was still served by make -ups consisting of a 

--- Document Chunk 3847 ---
diesel locomotive and Talgo coaches, as serving on the conventional line. Since this rolling stock did 

--- Document Chunk 3848 ---
not have on-board ERTMS, it ran under cover of ASFA Digital. 

--- Document Chunk 3849 ---
From 16 June 2012, this rolling stock was replaced with Class 730 railcar trains. These only ran f or a 

--- Document Chunk 3850 ---
week with ERTMS switched on. Then, in the early days of service, problems were detected with the 

--- Document Chunk 3851 ---
on-board ERTMS which had not been noticed during the complementary testing in February 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 3852 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 3853 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 3854 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 3855 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 3856 ---
MINISTRY OF

DEVELOPMENT

No 0054/2013, of 24.07.2013 

--- Document Chunk 3861 ---
Final Report RAILWAY ACCIDENTS 

--- Document Chunk 3862 ---
INVESTIGATION COMMISSION 

--- Document Chunk 3863 ---
ERA-2014-0070-00-00-ESEN 

--- Document Chunk 3864 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 3865 ---
Page 87 of 110 

--- Document Chunk 3866 ---
The reason for these problems was that the version 3.1.0.1 ER TMS installed on Class 730 trains made 

--- Document Chunk 3867 ---
by Bombardier had incompatibilities with the version installed on the track of line 082, made by Thales.  

--- Document Chunk 3868 ---
More specifically, one of the faults was failure to reach the first group of balises on track  1, Ourense 

--- Document Chunk 3869 ---
side, during changeover from ASFA to ERTMS, while bound for Santiago de Compostela. This meant 

--- Document Chunk 3870 ---
that, for one -fifth of the distance of line 082, the train was travelling in ‘driver’s responsibility’ mode, 

--- Document Chunk 3871 ---
without the complete supervision of ERTMS and without the p rotection of ASFA. This had traffic safety 

--- Document Chunk 3872 ---
implications. 

--- Document Chunk 3873 ---
That is why, on 23  June 2012, Renfe Operadora applied to Adif for authorisation for those trains on 

--- Document Chunk 3874 ---
line 082 to return to their previous conditions of travel, i.e. with ASFA Digital. This authorisati on was 

--- Document Chunk 3875 ---
granted on 25 June 2012. 

--- Document Chunk 3876 ---
To correct the reported defects and enable this rolling s tock to use line 082 with ERTMS, the 

--- Document Chunk 3877 ---
manufacturer (Bombardier) developed a new version of the software (version 3.1.1.2). It delivered the 

--- Document Chunk 3878 ---
documentation for this to Renfe Operadora in November 2012. Renfe Operadora arranged to carry out 

--- Document Chunk 3879 ---
the relevant trials on the track to check that it performed properly. The trials were carried out, with a 

--- Document Chunk 3880 ---
positive outcome, until April 2013. 

--- Document Chunk 3881 ---
Although the risk had been minimised, it was  still possible that the balises might not be read. Hence 

--- Document Chunk 3882 ---
the manufacturer’s proposed solution was to disable another of the on -board safety systems (EBICAB -

--- Document Chunk 3883 ---
ATP). This is being studied (March 2014). 

--- Document Chunk 3884 ---
While it is possible that the rolling stock involved in t he accident might have travelled with ERTMS in 

--- Document Chunk 3885 ---
its current configuration and extent (up to PK 80+069), this system would not have limited the speed 

--- Document Chunk 3886 ---
of entry to the Angrois bend because, from that point, it could travel at 200 km/h with ASFA. It would 

--- Document Chunk 3887 ---
still have been up to the driver to reduce speed, although he would have had to press the button 

--- Document Chunk 3888 ---
recognising exit from ERTMS on the cab DMI screen. In theory, this would have been one more factor 

--- Document Chunk 3889 ---
calling for attention during driving. If this had not been activa ted, the system would have applied the 

--- Document Chunk 3890 ---
service brake, which would have been released at the time of pressing the button. 

--- Document Chunk 3891 ---
Annex 3.4.3.6 contains Renfe Operadora’s application to run on ASFA and Adif’s authorisation to do 

--- Document Chunk 3892 ---
so. 

--- Document Chunk 3893 ---

3.5.2. Conversations between driver and Atocha Regulation and Control Centre  

--- Document Chunk 4057 ---
The Madrid -Atocha Regul ation and Control Centre (CRC), like the other control posts, records 

--- Document Chunk 4058 ---
conversations between itself and the drivers of the trains running in its territory. In this case, 

--- Document Chunk 4059 ---
conversations are by GSM-R telephony. 

--- Document Chunk 4060 ---
The recording of the conversations between the dr iver of train 150/151 and the Traffic Manager at 

--- Document Chunk 4061 ---
CRC Atocha has been extracted, from going on duty  at Ourense until the last recordings after the 

--- Document Chunk 4062 ---
accident. 

--- Document Chunk 4063 ---
Four conversations were held, all on channel  13. Start times were 20:02:04, 20:42:25, 20:46:53 and 

--- Document Chunk 4064 ---
21:10:06. The main points of each call are highlighted below. 

--- Document Chunk 4065 ---
 Conversation from 20:02:04 to 20:02:55 hours: 51 seconds’ duration 

--- Document Chunk 4066 ---
Driver of train 150/151 calls CRC from Ourense station to say that his name does not appear on the train 

--- Document Chunk 4067 ---
logbook, though it does not matter. CRC asks him if he is carrying the train log and if he is going on BSL 

--- Document Chunk 4068 ---
[i.e. without ERTMS but with ASFA]. Driver replies in the affirmative. 

--- Document Chunk 4069 ---
 Conversation from 20:42:25 to 20:42:57 hours: 32 seconds’ duration 

--- Document Chunk 4070 ---
Driver of train 150/151 calls CRC to say that there has been an accident. He has derailed, overturned 

--- Document Chunk 4071 ---
and is at kilometre 80. 

--- Document Chunk 4072 ---
 Conversation from 20:46:53 to 20:52:04 hours: 5 minutes 11 seconds’ duration 

--- Document Chunk 4073 ---
Driver calls CRC to report that there must be many injured because he has overturned. Cannot get out of 

--- Document Chunk 4074 ---
cab. Has derailed. Should have taken it at 80 [ km/h] but took it at 190. Had already told safety person 

--- Document Chunk 4075 ---
that it was dangerous and they would derail one day and it [the curve] would get the better of them. He 

--- Document Chunk 4076 ---
had been coming on green [with the signals at green]. The driver had to be there, but we are human.

--- Document Chunk 4101 ---
3.5.3. Regulations on communications in the cab  

--- Document Chunk 4102 ---
Chapter 15 of the Operation Manual deals with communication between the driver and the control 

--- Document Chunk 4103 ---
post. Communica tion is possible by radiotelephony (track -train) and, since the high -speed lines 

--- Document Chunk 4104 ---
opened, by mobile telephony (GSM-R), as in the case of line 082.  

--- Document Chunk 4105 ---
As regards the use of mobile telephones by driving staff, the existing regulations consist of Notice 102, 

--- Document Chunk 4106 ---
from the defunct RENFE, and Driver Information Sheet FIM 3, issued by Renfe Operadora.  

--- Document Chunk 4107 ---
The notice is published to give operating staff the necessary information about this. It is not a 

--- Document Chunk 4108 ---
regulation.  

--- Document Chunk 4109 ---
Notice 102 of the Directorate of Civil Defence and Traffic Sa fety, of 21  April 1997, reminds staff that, 

--- Document Chunk 4110 ---
due to the many means of communication in the cab, the driver must prioritise the use of the 

--- Document Chunk 4111 ---
radiotelephone system [track -train] and keep any other personal medium of communication switched 

--- Document Chunk 4112 ---
off. 

--- Document Chunk 4113 ---
The Technical Office for the Human Factor at Renfe Operadora was created in 2010. Its purpose is to 

--- Document Chunk 4114 ---
study the risks of the human factor and how to mitigate them. Most of these centre on driving. The 

--- Document Chunk 4115 ---
Office therefore studies the most common errors (real and potential) and b rings them to the attention 

--- Document Chunk 4116 ---
of those concerned (mainly drivers). It also forwards suitable recommendations on preventing them as 

--- Document Chunk 4117 ---
far as possible. All this information can be found in the FIM leaflets, which later provided input to the 

--- Document Chunk 4118 ---
Guide to Good Driving  Practice. This literature is for information; it is neither a regulation nor a 

--- Document Chunk 4119 ---
standard. 

--- Document Chunk 4120 ---
The use of mobile telephones and other electronic devices is widespread nowadays. They have also 

--- Document Chunk 4121 ---
been introduced to working activity on a wide scale. Hence FIM leafle t 3 on Safe Use of Mobile 

--- Document Chunk 4122 ---
Telephones while Driving , dated 18  July 2011, notes that using mobile telephones and other 

--- Document Chunk 4123 ---
communication devices may pose a risk, and recommends using them appropriately.  

--- Document Chunk 4124 ---
The leaflet says that, from the first minute of conversati on, the person becomes more involved in it 

--- Document Chunk 4125 ---
and relegates driving to second priority, not processing the information. One of the recommendations 

--- Document Chunk 4126 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4127 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4128 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4129 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 4130 ---

3.6. MAN-MACHINE INTERFACE OF STAFF INVOLVED 

--- Document Chunk 4144 ---
3.6.1. Working hours of staff involved 

--- Document Chunk 4145 ---
According to the report from Renfe Operadora, the driver in charge of train 150/151, involved in the 

--- Document Chunk 4146 ---
accident, is attached to the base in A Coruña. 

--- Document Chunk 4147 ---
On 24 July 2013 he had begun his working day at 11:55 hours in A Coruña, from where he travelled 

--- Document Chunk 4148 ---
off-duty to Pontevedra. At 14:42 hours he began his own work driving an Alvia 252 train from 

--- Document Chunk 4149 ---
Pontevedra to its destination at Madrid -Chamartín. He drove it to Ourense, where he arrived at 16:49. 

--- Document Chunk 4150 ---
He stayed there until 20:05, when he began driving duty on the train involved in the accident.  

--- Document Chunk 4151 ---
Therefore, by the time of the accident, his working day had been 8 hours 47 minutes. Actual driving  

--- Document Chunk 4152 ---
time had been 2 hours 44 minutes. He had taken the regulatory rest in the previous 48 hours.  

--- Document Chunk 4153 ---
Additional provision  11 of Royal Decree 2387/2004, approving the Rail Sector Regulation, sets a 

--- Document Chunk 4154 ---
maximum continuous driving period of 6 hours, and maximum driving in one day of 9 hours. 

--- Document Chunk 4155 ---
Likewise Royal Decree 1561/1995, of 21  September 1995, on extraordinary working days, establishes 

--- Document Chunk 4156 ---
a maximum working day of 12  hours and a minimum period of rest of one -and-a-half days per week. 

--- Document Chunk 4157 ---
The section on rail trans port establishes a maximum of nine  hours of actual ordinary working which 

--- Document Chunk 4158 ---
may, exceptionally, be exceeded.   

--- Document Chunk 4159 ---
Collective Bargaining Agreement II of Renfe Operadora also applies. The professional development 

--- Document Chunk 4160 ---
agreement (part on driving) deals with the working day, which it quantifies at 8 hours. This may rise to 

--- Document Chunk 4161 ---
9½ in specific cases. The agreement refers to the provision of the Single Driver Regulation (the recast 

--- Document Chunk 4162 ---
text of the Renfe Labour Regulation, Article 606). This specifies the content on maximum continuous 

--- Document Chunk 4163 ---
driving times, which it quantifies at 5½ hours. 

--- Document Chunk 4164 ---
All the periods worked by the driver (working day, driving and rest) were within the current 

--- Document Chunk 4165 ---
regulations. 

--- Document Chunk 4166 ---

3.6.3. Design of equipment with effects on anthropometric interface  

--- Document Chunk 4190 ---
The Class 730 rolling stock derives from Class 130, which was designed according to the regulations in 

--- Document Chunk 4191 ---
force at the time. Hence the technical regulations applicable to the 730 class has conti nued to be as 

--- Document Chunk 4192 ---
per the first interim provision of Order FOM/233/2006 (which governs conditions for approval of 

--- Document Chunk 4193 ---
railway rolling stock). More specifically, NTC MA -001 (technical requirements for conventional rolling 

--- Document Chunk 4194 ---
stock) and NTC MA-007 (conditions for variable-gauge axles to fulfil at speeds up to 250 km/h). 

--- Document Chunk 4195 ---
Annex 3.6.3 shows pictures of the driving desk of a driver’s cab of the 730 class. It shows parts of 

--- Document Chunk 4196 ---
the ‘dead man’ system, the brakes, ERTMS-ASFA Digital and communications.  

--- Document Chunk 4197 ---
This layout of the console on the Class 730 logically derives from that of the Class 130 rolling stock. 

--- Document Chunk 4198 ---
There have been very minor modifications (addition of diesel traction). The design of the Class 130 

--- Document Chunk 4199 ---
was based on the regulations existing at the time. Basically that meant UIC booklet 651 (drivers’ cabs), 

--- Document Chunk 4200 ---
to which NTC-MA-001 refers. 

--- Document Chunk 4201 ---
3.7. SIMILAR EVENTS IN THE PAST  

--- Document Chunk 4202 ---
Of the accidents and incidents known to CIAF, none has occurred either on line 082 Coto da Torre branch - 

--- Document Chunk 4203 ---

--- Document Chunk 4204 ---
Compostela where they connect with line 082.

--- Document Chunk 4206 ---

--- Document Chunk 4208 ---

--- Document Chunk 4209 ---
curve with a permanent speed limit of 90 km/h.

 Case 0013/2009.- Derailment on 23  February 2009, on the f ormer Feve network, involving a 

--- Document Chunk 4211 ---
passenger train near the Ozanes halt (Asturias), due to excess speed. It was going at 77  km/h round 

--- Document Chunk 4212 ---
a curve with a permanent speed limit of 40 km/h.

 Case 0028/2010.- Derailment on 14 June 2010, on the former Feve network, i nvolving a goods 

--- Document Chunk 4214 ---
train at Ortigueira (A Coruña), due to excess speed. It was going at 77  km/h round a curve wit h a 

--- Document Chunk 4215 ---
permanent speed limit of 60 km/h.  

--- Document Chunk 4216 ---
 Case 0038/2010.- Derailment on 14 July 2010, on the former Feve network, of a goods train at 

--- Document Chunk 4217 ---
Ribadeo (A Co ruña), due to excess speed. It was going at 73  km/h round a curve with a permanent 

--- Document Chunk 4218 ---

 Case 0012/2013. - Derailment on 31  January 2013, on the former Feve network, involving a

--- Document Chunk 4240 ---
Thus this Commission has investigated six events: one on the Adif network and five on the Feve 

--- Document Chunk 4241 ---
network. All occurred on curves with perm anent speed limits, duly signalled on the track according to 

--- Document Chunk 4242 ---
the regulations. ASFA balises were not set up on any of these, because they are not mandatory with 

--- Document Chunk 4243 ---
permanent speed limits. 

--- Document Chunk 4244 ---
The recommendations issued by CIAF to Feve basically sought to reinforce  action to avoid risky 

--- Document Chunk 4245 ---
behaviour by driving staff. 

--- Document Chunk 4246 ---
Adif was also requested to report events (accidents and incidents) occurring on its rail network due to 

--- Document Chunk 4247 ---
excessive speed. 

--- Document Chunk 4248 ---
From 2005 until 24 July 2013, there were 20 events (14 incidents and 6 accidents) fo r which the main 

--- Document Chunk 4249 ---
cause was classed as excess speed. Only two of these (accidents) occurred on curves (one was on 

--- Document Chunk 4250 ---
5 July 2008 at Medina del Campo, investigated by this Commission, and the other was the accident 

--- Document Chunk 4251 ---
reported on here, of 24 July 2013). 

--- Document Chunk 4252 ---
Another five (four incidents and one accident) occurred in temporary speed limits (due to works or the 

--- Document Chunk 4253 ---
state of the infrastructure). The 13 remaining (10  incidents and 3  accidents) occurred while passing 

--- Document Chunk 4254 ---
track equipment (bypasses and crossovers). 

--- Document Chunk 4255 ---
To sum up, none of the events investigated by this Commission or occurring on the Adif network 

--- Document Chunk 4256 ---
(since 2005) have had features similar to the Santiago de Compostela derailment, i.e. exceeding the 

--- Document Chunk 4257 ---
maximum speed prescribed for the route in the Maximum Speed Table and in the timetable. 

--- Document Chunk 4258 ---

--- Document Chunk 4261 ---

--- Document Chunk 4302 ---
that this had been passed and regained speed.

--- Document Chunk 4304 ---

Atocha Regulation and Control Centre (CRC). The conversation lasted 32  seconds and he reported

what had happened. Later two more conversations were held. 

--- Document Chunk 4430 ---
Both main tracks of line 082 were blocked at the A Grandeira branch. A third track, which starts at that 

--- Document Chunk 4431 ---
point, next to the others but belonging to line 822 (Zamora - A Coruña), was also treated as out of 

--- Document Chunk 4432 ---
service, to facilitate the work of assistance and repair, although this third track was not affected by the 

--- Document Chunk 4433 ---
accident. 

--- Document Chunk 4434 ---
Track 2 was not opened to traffic until 26 July and track 1 remained closed until 29 July.

--- Document Chunk 4439 ---
reduce speed norm ally at caution signal E´7 [located at PK 80+619], but that day he took it [the 

--- Document Chunk 4440 ---
bend] at around 190 km/h.

(timetable book). 

--- Document Chunk 4444 ---

--- Document Chunk 4445 ---

--- Document Chunk 4446 ---

--- Document Chunk 4448 ---

--- Document Chunk 4515 ---

--- Document Chunk 4516 ---

 The regulations applicable from Coto da Torre branch to A Grandeira branch point at km 85.0, 

--- Document Chunk 4518 ---
the section where the accident occurred, are the Technical and Operating Requirements (the ‘PTOs"). 

--- Document Chunk 4519 ---
 The new line 082, from PK 80.1 (end of ERTMS and start of ASFA) to PK 85.0 (end of line and 

--- Document Chunk 4520 ---
junction with line 822 a t Santiago station), only has ASFA (as its main syst em). This is the stretch 

--- Document Chunk 4521 ---
where the accident occurred. 

--- Document Chunk 4522 ---
 The safety case documentation for the C ommand/Control and Signalling subsystem on the new 

--- Document Chunk 4523 ---
line 082 (these include the ‘safety file’) includes a risk assessment. This identifies the risks and 

--- Document Chunk 4524 ---
considers that those which cannot be covered by the specific subsystem should be exported to other 

--- Document Chunk 4525 ---
environments. These environments then take over the risks according to the established rules (at least 

--- Document Chunk 4526 ---
those relating to the circumstances of this accident).  

--- Document Chunk 4527 ---
To be specific, and with direct application to this accident, the safety case states that ‘trains travelling 

--- Document Chunk 4528 ---
under cover of the lateral signalling or ASFA (as is the case) shall comply with the Maximum Speed 

--- Document Chunk 4529 ---
Table for the line issued by Adif. This risk shall be exported to the driver.’ 

--- Document Chunk 4530 ---
So the risk assessment in the strict sense is applied to this subsystem (command/control and 

--- Document Chunk 4531 ---
signalling). The remaining subsystems are governed by other risk acceptance principles. A joint 

--- Document Chunk 4532 ---
analysis is therefore appropriate, taking acc ount of the interaction between subsystems 

--- Document Chunk 4533 ---
(Recommendation 5).  

--- Document Chunk 4534 ---
 The last dynamic examination, in May  2013, yielded figures indicating that the track was in 

--- Document Chunk 4535 ---
good condition on the stretch where the accident took place. This finding was corroborated by 

--- Document Chunk 4536 ---
collection of field data from the track. All values were within tolerance.  

--- Document Chunk 4537 ---
 The maximum permitted speed on the Angrois bend (80  km/h) is reflected in the Maximum 

--- Document Chunk 4538 ---
Speed Table and train timetable. It is compatible with the horizontal layout and camber of the curve.  

--- Document Chunk 4539 ---

--- Document Chunk 4540 ---
mode, RGC and speed reduction) comply, in both location and content, with the requirements of the 

--- Document Chunk 4541 ---
PTOs. In fact the PTOs do not require prior, fixed trackside signa lling of downward changes in 

--- Document Chunk 4542 ---
maximum speed.
