With regard to the rolling stock involved in the accident [section 3.4.3] 

--- Document Chunk 4558 ---
It was functioning properly: 

--- Document Chunk 4559 ---
 Rake 730.012, involved in the accident, had received authorisations for commissioning and 

--- Document Chunk 4560 ---
running. 

--- Document Chunk 4561 ---
 It had an approved maintenance plan. Approved contractors had carried out all servicing required 

--- Document Chunk 4562 ---
by that plan, at authorised centres. 

--- Document Chunk 4563 ---
 The fault logs for the tractor units of the trainset involved in the accident contained no notes of 

--- Document Chunk 4564 ---
outstanding brake defects. 

--- Document Chunk 4565 ---
 The figures for running the whole make -up were within the limits set by the maintenance plan 

--- Document Chunk 4566 ---
and by the regulations. 

--- Document Chunk 4567 ---
 The brake test, carried out at Ourense, showed that rake 012, involved in the accident, had 

--- Document Chunk 4568 ---
braking on all its axles and wheelsets. An estimate of the deceleration achieved by the emergency 

--- Document Chunk 4569 ---
braking, carried out moments before the derailment, yields values commensurate with the provisions 

--- Document Chunk 4570 ---
of the Rolling Stock TSI. 

--- Document Chunk 4571 ---
 Due to ERTMS problems from June  2012, the rolling stock was a uthorised to run with th e ASFA 

--- Document Chunk 4572 ---
Digital system switched on throughout the length of line 082. ERTMS was not active at any time on 

--- Document Chunk 4573 ---
the Ourense-Santiago stretch. The train was therefore running under cover of lateral signal blocking, 

--- Document Chunk 4574 ---
at the then maximum permitted speed of 200 km/h. This was still so in March 2014. 

--- Document Chunk 4575 ---
Therefore the decision taken at the time to modify the physical extent of the ERTMS bore no direct 

--- Document Chunk 4576 ---
relation to the specific causes established for this accident. The incompatibilities which obliged this train 

--- Document Chunk 4577 ---
to travel on BSL and ASFA might have arisen even if the ERTMS had covered Santiago de Compostela 

--- Document Chunk 4578 ---
station. 

--- Document Chunk 4579 ---
While it is possible that the rolling stock involved in the accident could have travelled with ERTMS at its 

--- Document Chunk 4580 ---
current extent (up to PK 80+069) and configuration, this  system would not have limited the speed of 

--- Document Chunk 4581 ---
entry to the Angrois bend. This was because, from that point, the train could travel at 200  km/h with 

--- Document Chunk 4582 ---
ASFA. It was the driver who had to reduce speed, although he would have to have noticed in the cab 

--- Document Chunk 4583 ---
that the tr ain had left the ERTMS. Theoretically, this would have been one more factor focusing his 

--- Document Chunk 4584 ---
attention on driving. If this had gone unnoticed, the system would have turned on the brakes.  

--- Document Chunk 4585 ---
 The data log from the safety recorder on the head locomotive of the train involved in the accident 

--- Document Chunk 4586 ---
makes it clear that it left Ourense four minutes late, at 20:05 hours. It was travelling normally, 

--- Document Chunk 4587 ---
reaching its maximum speed of 200 km/h around 20:23 hours, having passed all signals at green.  

--- Document Chunk 4588 ---
It did not start braking at PK 80+619 (signal E´7 to adjust to the 80 km/h limit at PK 84+230 - start of 

--- Document Chunk 4589 ---
the Angrois bend). Instead, it maintained a speed of nearly 200  km/h up to PK 84+009. Here, the 

--- Document Chunk 4590 ---
emergency brake was applied. It entered the Angrois bend practically at this speed. It was  derailed

--- Document Chunk 4651 ---
4.3. CONCLUSIONS 

--- Document Chunk 4652 ---
Consequently, in view of the description of events and taking the earlier considerations into account,  

--- Document Chunk 4653 ---
together with the special reports from Adif and Renfe Operadora, the chief investigator concludes 

--- Document Chunk 4654 ---
that: 

--- Document Chunk 4655 ---
The cause of the accident was excessiv e speed of the train (going at 179  km/h) on the curve entering 

--- Document Chunk 4656 ---
the A Grandeira bran ch (Angrois bend, limited to 80  km/h). The driver was in breach of the 

--- Document Chunk 4657 ---
requirement of the timetable book for train 150/151 and the maximum speed table for line 082.  

--- Document Chunk 4658 ---
As a con tributory cause, we note that the driver was distracted by answering an internal telephone 

--- Document Chunk 4659 ---
call from the train manager on his own train, which explains why he did not brake hard enough to 

--- Document Chunk 4660 ---
reduce speed before entering that curve. 

--- Document Chunk 4661 ---
4.4. FURTHER FINDINGS 

--- Document Chunk 4662 ---
Minor disc repancies have been found between the set timetable for train 150/151, the Maximum 

--- Document Chunk 4663 ---
Speed Table for line 082 and the practical arrangements (relating to the scope of the ERTMS). These 

--- Document Chunk 4664 ---
discrepancies are unrelated to the accident causes. 

--- Document Chunk 4665 ---
5. MEASURES ADOPTED 

--- Document Chunk 4666 ---
5.1. GENERAL MEASURES 

--- Document Chunk 4667 ---
5.1.1. Proposals by the Railway Accident Investigation Commission (CIAF)  

--- Document Chunk 4668 ---
Based on the analysis of the facts of what had happened, completed by that date, the plenary 

--- Document Chunk 4669 ---
meeting of the CIAF, on 30  July 2013, agreed to issue advance safety recommendation s which, if and 

--- Document Chunk 4670 ---
when possible, were to include this report when completed.  

--- Document Chunk 4671 ---
The purpose of those preliminary recommendations was to avoid possible repetition of the situation of 

--- Document Chunk 4672 ---
the Santiago accident. They were submitted to the Directorate -General of Railw ays (DGF), as the 

--- Document Chunk 4673 ---
national rail safety authority, on  1 August 2013. DGF then forwarded them to Adif, which was 

--- Document Chunk 4674 ---
competent for them. They are as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 4675 ---
1.-  Ensure that all reductions of maximum speed programmed on the main track between stations, 

--- Document Chunk 4676 ---
from a certain deceleration, are signed on the track. 

--- Document Chunk 4677 ---
2.-  In these situations, arrange progressive set -up of ASFA balises which check train speeds and 

--- Document Chunk 4678 ---
ensure immediate braking if the maximum speed of entry to the next track section is lower.  

--- Document Chunk 4679 ---
5.1.2. Measures announced by the Ministry of Development 

--- Document Chunk 4680 ---
The Minister of Development attended the meeting of the Development Commission o f the Congress 

--- Document Chunk 4681 ---
of Deputies on 9 August 2013 about this accident. She has planned a set of 20 measures which tackle 

--- Document Chunk 4682 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4683 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4684 ---
 

--- Document Chunk 4685 ---
A 

--- Document Chunk 4686 ---
MINISTRY OF 

--- Document Chunk 4687 ---

--- Document Chunk 4696 ---
various aspects of the rail sect or, with a view to improving it and setting out lines of action for the 

--- Document Chunk 4697 ---
future.  

--- Document Chunk 4698 ---
The measures she announced relate to improving infrastructure (signalling), personnel (selection and 

--- Document Chunk 4699 ---
training), rolling stock, passengers (improving passenger management) and regulations. As of 

--- Document Chunk 4700 ---
March 2014 the list of these measures, including action on the CIAF preliminary recommendations 

--- Document Chunk 4701 ---
referred to above, was as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 4702 ---
1.- Revise the maximum speed tables for all lines, with speed graduation analysis, and setting criteria 

--- Document Chunk 4703 ---
for variation of the maximum speeds. 

--- Document Chunk 4704 ---
Those tables, and the existing speed transitions, have been revised. A definition has been reached for  

--- Document Chunk 4705 ---
a ‘significant change of speed ’, which has been detected at 375 points on the Adif network (51 on 

--- Document Chunk 4706 ---
high-speed lines and 324 on the conventional network). 

--- Document Chunk 4707 ---
2.- Revise the signalling on the track of the lines identified by the above analysis, which are not 

--- Document Chunk 4708 ---
marked with any other type of sign. This will be done by signs warning of a change of speed, and of 

--- Document Chunk 4709 ---
the commencement of that speed. 

--- Document Chunk 4710 ---
Signs have already been set up at 122 significant changes of speed, where the speed difference is at 

--- Document Chunk 4711 ---
least 40% of the lower speed. These are either on high -speed lines (37) or on lines belonging to the 

--- Document Chunk 4712 ---
conventional network with maximum speed over 160 km/h (85). 

--- Document Chunk 4713 ---
3.- Provide protection, by means of a set of ASFA balises, on the sections where there is a significant 

--- Document Chunk 4714 ---
reduction of the maximum speed, like the protection for temporary speed limits on the track.  

--- Document Chunk 4715 ---
The 122 significant changes of speed above already have balises. 

--- Document Chunk 4716 ---
4.- Work with the industry to promote further development of ASFA Digital so that it has greater 

--- Document Chunk 4717 ---
capacity to transmit information from track to train, allows greater versatility, and offers the possibility 

--- Document Chunk 4718 ---
of transmitting voice signals in addition to acoustic signals, as at present. 

--- Document Chunk 4719 ---
The development framework for ASFA Digital (already fitted to most rolling stock) includes a plan for on-

--- Document Chunk 4720 ---
track trials of the new prototype 11-frequency balise (analogue ASFA currently offers five). Some of the 

--- Document Chunk 4721 ---
new frequencies will be allocated to speed control.  

--- Document Chunk 4722 ---
5.- Analyse the engineering rules of the technical procedures for transition from ERTMS to ASFA.  

--- Document Chunk 4723 ---
This measure has already been finalised. The applicable rules have been reviewed and analysed, in 

--- Document Chunk 4724 ---
addition to the conditions on which each existing transition is carried out in the infrastructure. The 

--- Document Chunk 4725 ---
study was limited to scheduled and automatic transitions between ERTMS Level 1 and ASFA. It did not 

--- Document Chunk 4726 ---
include manual transitions or transitions degraded due to malfunctioning. 

--- Document Chunk 4727 ---
6.- Explore in depth the possibility of installing a satellite system for trains as back -up to the signalling 

--- Document Chunk 4728 ---
systems. 

--- Document Chunk 4729 ---

The Ministry of Development and Renfe Operadora have signed a co -operation agreement with the 

--- Document Chunk 4757 ---
Official Board of Psychologists to analyse the psychological aspects of driving. 

--- Document Chunk 4758 ---
10.- Write down the procedure for going on duty each day at the start of work, which the driver has 

--- Document Chunk 4759 ---
to check with the management centre. 

--- Document Chunk 4760 ---
This means setting up a formal verification procedure in the form of a checklist for drivers to complete at 

--- Document Chunk 4761 ---
the beginning, handover and end of duty, leaving a record of possible incidents. There is already a file for a 

--- Document Chunk 4762 ---
checking procedure for long and medium-distance goods and passengers. 

--- Document Chunk 4763 ---
11.- Assess the possibility of recording work in progress on trains. 

--- Document Chunk 4764 ---
Install audio and video  recording systems in the cab, but restrict their use to accident or incident 

--- Document Chunk 4765 ---
investigations alone. A technical specification has been drawn up about this. New trains must conform 

--- Document Chunk 4766 ---
to it.  

--- Document Chunk 4767 ---
12.- Revise the rules on the use of (mobile) communication equipment  by staff on board trains. A 

--- Document Chunk 4768 ---
single, integrated system of communication will be set up, so that the driver can activate 

--- Document Chunk 4769 ---
communication via a hands-free system. 

--- Document Chunk 4770 ---
This means regulating the safe use of the communication technology and appliance in the cab, and 

--- Document Chunk 4771 ---
including them in a single system which allows hands -free mode. Renfe Operadora has issued Circular 

--- Document Chunk 4772 ---
Resolution 3 on ‘Proper use of communication devices and electronic appliances during train driving 

--- Document Chunk 4773 ---
and manoeuvres,’ dated 28 February 2014. This prohibits mobile telephone use by drivers, except in 

--- Document Chunk 4774 ---
cases of communication failure or emergency. This applies not only to drivers, but to all personnel 

--- Document Chunk 4775 ---
who have relations with drivers.

5.2. SPECIFIC MEASURES IN THE ACCIDENT ZONE OF LINE 082 

--- Document Chunk 4857 ---
On 13 August 2013, after the accident, Adif installed signage corresponding to two temporary speed limits 

--- Document Chunk 4858 ---
on track 1 of line 082 heading towards Santiago de Compostela, and near Angrois. These were 160 km/h, 

--- Document Chunk 4859 ---
with signs in the run-up (PK 78+778) and at the start of the restriction (PK 80+338); and 30 km/h (initially 

--- Document Chunk 4860 ---
due to the repair of this track after the accident), and also with signs in the run-up (PK 81+669) and at the 

--- Document Chunk 4861 ---
start of the restriction (PK 84+400). A balise was also set up with the sign announcing the temporary 

--- Document Chunk 4862 ---
30 km/h speed limit. These signs remained in place on track 1 in March 2014.  

--- Document Chunk 4863 ---
In the same direction on track 2 (Ourense -Santiago), signs were also set up on the Angrois bend as a 

--- Document Chunk 4864 ---
permanent speed limit. There was a sign giving advance notice of the speed restriction (as the speed 

--- Document Chunk 4865 ---
was greater than 160  km/h) and signs giving warning, and at the start, of the 80  km/h speed limit. 

--- Document Chunk 4866 ---
These signs were backed by a balise at the pre-warning sign.

6. RECOMMENDATIONS 

--- Document Chunk 4882 ---
The recommendations proposed below result from the technical investigation into the accident. Some 

--- Document Chunk 4883 ---
tend to reinforce the measures announced by the Ministry of Development, as mentioned.  

--- Document Chunk 4884 ---
Final addressee Number Recommendation 

--- Document Chunk 4885 ---
Adif 54/13-1 

--- Document Chunk 4886 ---
Make it a rule that all speed reductions, from a certain 

--- Document Chunk 4887 ---
deceleration onwards, must be marked on the track by 

--- Document Chunk 4888 ---
fixed speed limit signs.  

--- Document Chunk 4889 ---
Adif 54/13-2 

--- Document Chunk 4890 ---
For these situations (significant speed reductions), 

--- Document Chunk 4891 ---
arrange progressive set-up of balises which may help to 

--- Document Chunk 4892 ---
control the speed of trains, so that they brake in case the 

--- Document Chunk 4893 ---
speed limit for entry into the next section is lowered. 

--- Document Chunk 4894 ---
Therefore, implement the necessary ASFA Digital 

--- Document Chunk 4895 ---
(Automatic Braking and Announcement of Signals) 

--- Document Chunk 4896 ---
systems.  

--- Document Chunk 4897 ---
Renfe Operadora 54/13-3.1 

--- Document Chunk 4898 ---
Reinforce the procedures set in the Renfe Operadora SMS 

--- Document Chunk 4899 ---
so that safety -related defects detected at any level are 

--- Document Chunk 4900 ---
referred to the departments with the prescribed function 

--- Document Chunk 4901 ---
of analysing and considering them, thereby assuring  

--- Document Chunk 4902 ---
effective preventive management. 

--- Document Chunk 4903 ---
DGF 54/13-3.2 

--- Document Chunk 4904 ---
The national railway safety authority  will ensure that 

--- Document Chunk 4905 ---
Recommendation 54/13 -3.1 is extended to the other 

--- Document Chunk 4906 ---
railway undertakings. 

--- Document Chunk 4907 ---
DGF 54/13-4 

--- Document Chunk 4908 ---
The national railway safety authority  should con sider 

--- Document Chunk 4909 ---
whether to re convene the Joint Traffic Safety 

--- Document Chunk 4910 ---
Committees, including representatives from Adif and the 

--- Document Chunk 4911 ---
railway undertakings, and under the authority’s 

--- Document Chunk 4912 ---
supervision. These committees can analyse risk situations 

--- Document Chunk 4913 ---
deriving from the interaction between driving, vehicle and 

--- Document Chunk 4914 ---
track.

--- Document Chunk 4935 ---

--- Document Chunk 4939 ---

--- Document Chunk 4941 ---
